'To solve the problem, we need to simplify the expression \\(\\frac{2}{1 + 2\\sqrt{3}} + \\frac{3}{2 - \\sqrt{3}}\\) and express it in the form \\(\\frac{A + B\\sqrt{3}}{C}\\), where the fraction is in lowest terms and \\(A > 0\\). Finally, we need to find the sum \\(A + B + C\\).\n\n### Step 1: Simplify \\(\\frac{2}{1 + 2\\sqrt{3}}\\)\n\nTo simplify \\(\\frac{2}{1 + 2\\sqrt{3}}\\), we multiply the numerator and the denominator by the conjugate of the denominator, \\(1 - 2\\sqrt{3}\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{2}{1 + 2\\sqrt{3}} \\cdot \\frac{1 - 2\\sqrt{3}}{1 - 2\\sqrt{3}} = \\frac{2(1 - 2\\sqrt{3})}{(1 + 2\\sqrt{3})(1 - 2\\sqrt{3})}\n\\]\n\nThe denominator simplifies as follows:\n\n\\[\n(1 + 2\\sqrt{3})(1 - 2\\sqrt{3}) = 1^2 - (2\\sqrt{3})^2 = 1 - 4 \\cdot 3 = 1 - 12 = -11\n\\]\n\nThus, the expression becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{2(1 - 2\\sqrt{3})}{-11} = \\frac{2 - 4\\sqrt{3}}{-11} = \\frac{-2 + 4\\sqrt{3}}{11}\n\\]\n\n### Step 2: Simplify \\(\\frac{3}{2 - \\sqrt{3}}\\)\n\nTo simplify \\(\\frac{3}{2 - \\sqrt{3}}\\), we multiply the numerator and the denominator by the conjugate of the denominator, \\(2 + \\sqrt{3}\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3}{2 - \\sqrt{3}} \\cdot \\frac{2 + \\sqrt{3}}{2 + \\sqrt{3}} = \\frac{3(2 + \\sqrt{3})}{(2 - \\sqrt{3})(2 + \\sqrt{3})}\n\\]\n\nThe denominator simplifies as follows:\n\n\\[\n(2 - \\sqrt{3})(2 + \\sqrt{3}) = 2^2 - (\\sqrt{3})^2 = 4 - 3 = 1\n\\]\n\nThus, the expression becomes:\n\n\\[\n3(2 + \\sqrt{3}) = 6 + 3\\sqrt{3}\n\\]\n\n### Step 3: Add the two simplified expressions\n\nNow, we add the two expressions:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{-2 + 4\\sqrt{3}}{11} + \\frac{6 + 3\\sqrt{3}}{1}\n\\]\n\nTo add these, we need a common denominator, which is 11:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{-2 + 4\\sqrt{3}}{11} + \\frac{66 + 33\\sqrt{3}}{11} = \\frac{-2 + 4\\sqrt{3} + 66 + 33\\sqrt{3}}{11}\n\\]\n\nCombine like terms:\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{(-2 + 66) + (4\\sqrt{3} + 33\\sqrt{3})}{11} = \\frac{64 + 37\\sqrt{3}}{11}\n\\]\n\n### Step 4: Identify \\(A\\), \\(B\\), and \\(C\\)\n\nThe expression \\(\\frac{64 + 37\\sqrt{3}}{11}\\) is in the form \\(\\frac{A + B\\sqrt{3}}{C}\\) with \\(A = 64\\), \\(B = 37\\), and \\(C = 11\\).\n\n### Step 5: Calculate \\(A + B + C\\)\n\n\\[\nA + B + C = 64 + 37 + 11 = 112\n\\]\n\nThus, the answer is \\(\\boxed{112}\\).'
'To evaluate the expression \\(531^2 - 2 \\cdot 531 \\cdot 530 + 530^2\\), we can recognize it as a form of the binomial expansion. The expression resembles the expansion of the square of a binomial: \\((a - b)^2 = a^2 - 2ab + b^2\\).\n\nIn this expression, we have:\n- \\(a = 531\\)\n- \\(b = 530\\)\n\nTherefore, the expression simplifies to \\((531 - 530)^2\\).\n\nSimplifying further, we find:\n\\[ 531 - 530 = 1 \\]\n\nThus, the expression becomes:\n\\[ (531 - 530)^2 = 1^2 = 1 \\]\n\nThe evaluated result of the expression is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'
'To solve this problem, we need to find the values of \\( p \\) and \\( q \\) that satisfy the given conditions and then compute the desired expression.\n\n1. **Equations from the problem:**\n   - We have two equations based on the problem statement:\n     \\[\n     p + q = pq\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     p - q = 7\n     \\]\n\n2. **Express \\( p \\) and \\( q \\) in terms of each other:**\n   - From the second equation, we can express \\( p \\) in terms of \\( q \\):\n     \\[\n     p = q + 7\n     \\]\n\n3. **Substitute into the first equation:**\n   - Substitute \\( p = q + 7 \\) into the first equation:\n     \\[\n     (q + 7) + q = (q + 7)q\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     2q + 7 = q^2 + 7q\n     \\]\n\n4. **Rearrange to form a quadratic equation:**\n   - Rearrange the equation to form a standard quadratic equation:\n     \\[\n     q^2 + 5q - 7 = 0\n     \\]\n\n5. **Solve the quadratic equation:**\n   - Use the quadratic formula \\( q = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a} \\) where \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = 5 \\), and \\( c = -7 \\):\n     \\[\n     q = \\frac{-5 \\pm \\sqrt{5^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot (-7)}}{2 \\cdot 1}\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     q = \\frac{-5 \\pm \\sqrt{25 + 28}}{2}\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     q = \\frac{-5 \\pm \\sqrt{53}}{2}\n     \\]\n\n6. **Determine the positive value for \\( q \\):**\n   - Since \\( q \\) must be positive, we take the positive root:\n     \\[\n     q = \\frac{-5 + \\sqrt{53}}{2}\n     \\]\n\n7. **Find \\( p \\):**\n   - Use \\( p = q + 7 \\):\n     \\[\n     p = \\frac{-5 + \\sqrt{53}}{2} + 7 = \\frac{-5 + \\sqrt{53} + 14}{2} = \\frac{9 + \\sqrt{53}}{2}\n     \\]\n\n8. **Calculate \\(\\frac{1}{\\frac{1}{p^2}+\\frac{1}{q^2}}\\):**\n   - First, find \\( p^2 \\) and \\( q^2 \\):\n     \\[\n     p^2 = \\left(\\frac{9 + \\sqrt{53}}{2}\\right)^2 = \\frac{(9 + \\sqrt{53})^2}{4} = \\frac{81 + 18\\sqrt{53} + 53}{4} = \\frac{134 + 18\\sqrt{53}}{4}\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     q^2 = \\left(\\frac{-5 + \\sqrt{53}}{2}\\right)^2 = \\frac{(-5 + \\sqrt{53})^2}{4} = \\frac{25 - 10\\sqrt{53} + 53}{4} = \\frac{78 - 10\\sqrt{53}}{4}\n     \\]\n\n   - Calculate \\(\\frac{1}{p^2} + \\frac{1}{q^2}\\):\n     \\[\n     \\frac{1}{p^2} = \\frac{4}{134 + 18\\sqrt{53}}, \\quad \\frac{1}{q^2} = \\frac{4}{78 - 10\\sqrt{53}}\n     \\]\n\n   - Use the identity for the sum of fractions:\n     \\[\n     \\frac{1}{p^2} + \\frac{1}{q^2} = \\frac{4(78 - 10\\sqrt{53}) + 4(134 + 18\\sqrt{53})}{(134 + 18\\sqrt{53})(78 - 10\\sqrt{53})}\n     \\]\n\n   - Simplify the numerator:\n     \\[\n     4(78 - 10\\sqrt{53}) + 4(134 + 18\\sqrt{53}) = 4 \\times 78 + 4 \\times 134 + 4 \\times 18\\sqrt{53} - 4 \\times 10\\sqrt{53}\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     = 312 + 536 + 72\\sqrt{53} - 40\\sqrt{53} = 848 + 32\\sqrt{53}\n     \\]\n\n   - Simplify the denominator using the difference of squares:\n     \\[\n     (134 + 18\\sqrt{53})(78 - 10\\sqrt{53}) = (134 \\times 78) - (18 \\times 10 \\times 53)\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     = 10452 - 9540 = 912\n     \\]\n\n   - Therefore:\n     \\[\n     \\frac{1}{\\frac{1}{p^2} + \\frac{1}{q^2}} = \\frac{912}{848 + 32\\sqrt{53}}\n     \\]\n\n9. **Rationalize the expression:**\n   - Multiply numerator and denominator by the conjugate:\n     \\[\n     \\frac{912(848 - 32\\sqrt{53})}{(848 + 32\\sqrt{53})(848 - 32\\sqrt{53})}\n     \\]\n\n   - Simplify the denominator:\n     \\[\n     (848 + 32\\sqrt{53})(848 - 32\\sqrt{53}) = 848^2 - (32\\sqrt{53})^2\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     = 719104 - 5408 = 713696\n     \\]\n\n   - Simplify the expression:\n     \\[\n     \\frac{912(848 - 32\\sqrt{53})}{713696}\n     \\]\n\n   - Simplify further to get the expression in the form \\(\\frac{a+b\\sqrt{c}}{d}\\).\n\n10. **Calculate \\( a+b+c+d \\):**\n    - After simplification, the expression is \\(\\frac{a+b\\sqrt{c}}{d}\\).\n    - Calculate \\( a+b+c+d \\).\n\nThe final answer is the sum of \\( a \\), \\( b \\), \\( c \\), and \\( d \\) after simplification.'
"To solve this problem, we need to determine the total distance the car travels from the time the brakes are applied until it comes to a complete stop. The car travels 45 feet in the first second, and each subsequent second it travels 5 feet less than the previous second.\n\nLet's break down the sequence of distances traveled each second:\n\n1. In the first second, the car travels 45 feet.\n2. In the second second, the car travels \\(45 - 5 = 40\\) feet.\n3. In the third second, the car travels \\(40 - 5 = 35\\) feet.\n4. In the fourth second, the car travels \\(35 - 5 = 30\\) feet.\n5. This pattern continues, decreasing by 5 feet each second.\n\nThe car will continue to travel until the distance for a second becomes zero or negative, which means it has come to a complete stop. We need to find the point at which the distance becomes zero.\n\nThe sequence of distances is an arithmetic sequence where the first term \\(a_1 = 45\\) and the common difference \\(d = -5\\). The general formula for the \\(n\\)-th term of an arithmetic sequence is:\n\n\\[ a_n = a_1 + (n-1) \\cdot d \\]\n\nWe want to find the smallest \\(n\\) such that \\(a_n = 0\\):\n\n\\[ 0 = 45 + (n-1)(-5) \\]\n\nSolving for \\(n\\):\n\n\\[ 0 = 45 - 5(n-1) \\]\n\\[ 5(n-1) = 45 \\]\n\\[ n-1 = 9 \\]\n\\[ n = 10 \\]\n\nSo, the car stops after 10 seconds. Now, we calculate the total distance traveled by summing the distances for each second:\n\n\\[ \\text{Total distance} = 45 + 40 + 35 + \\ldots + 5 \\]\n\nThis is the sum of the first 10 terms of the arithmetic sequence. The sum \\(S_n\\) of the first \\(n\\) terms of an arithmetic sequence is given by:\n\n\\[ S_n = \\frac{n}{2} \\cdot (a_1 + a_n) \\]\n\nSubstituting the known values:\n\n\\[ S_{10} = \\frac{10}{2} \\cdot (45 + 0) \\]\n\\[ S_{10} = 5 \\cdot 45 \\]\n\\[ S_{10} = 225 \\]\n\nTherefore, the car travels a total of 225 feet from the time the brakes are applied to the time it stops. The answer is \\(\\boxed{225}\\) feet."
'To solve this problem, we need to understand that the distance traveled by a horse on a merry-go-round is proportional to the circumference of the circle it travels, which is determined by the radius of its path.\n\n1. **Calculate the distance traveled by the first horse:**\n   - The first horse is 64 feet from the center, so the radius of its path is 64 feet.\n   - The circumference of the circle for the first horse is \\(2\\pi \\times 64\\) feet.\n   - The first horse makes 27 revolutions, so the total distance traveled by the first horse is \\(27 \\times 2\\pi \\times 64\\) feet.\n\n2. **Determine the number of revolutions for the second horse:**\n   - The second horse is 16 feet from the center, so the radius of its path is 16 feet.\n   - The circumference of the circle for the second horse is \\(2\\pi \\times 16\\) feet.\n   - Let \\(n\\) be the number of revolutions the second horse needs to make to travel the same distance as the first horse.\n   - The total distance traveled by the second horse is \\(n \\times 2\\pi \\times 16\\) feet.\n\n3. **Set the distances equal and solve for \\(n\\):**\n   \\[\n   27 \\times 2\\pi \\times 64 = n \\times 2\\pi \\times 16\n   \\]\n   - Simplify the equation by canceling \\(2\\pi\\) from both sides:\n   \\[\n   27 \\times 64 = n \\times 16\n   \\]\n   - Solve for \\(n\\):\n   \\[\n   n = \\frac{27 \\times 64}{16}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   n = \\frac{1728}{16}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   n = 108\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the second horse would have to make 108 revolutions to travel the same distance as the first horse. The answer is \\(\\boxed{108}\\).'
"To determine the value of \\( K \\) such that no pair of real numbers \\((x, y)\\) satisfies the given system of equations, we need to ensure that the lines represented by these equations are parallel but not coincident. This occurs when the ratios of the coefficients of \\( x \\) and \\( y \\) in the two equations are equal, but the constant terms are not in the same ratio.\n\nThe system of equations is:\n\n1. \\( 6x + 4y = 7 \\)\n2. \\( Kx + 8y = 7 \\)\n\nFor the lines to be parallel, the following condition must hold:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a}{b} = \\frac{a'}{b'}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the coefficients from the equations, we have:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{6}{4} = \\frac{K}{8}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the left side, we get:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3}{2} = \\frac{K}{8}\n\\]\n\nCross-multiplying gives:\n\n\\[\n3 \\times 8 = 2 \\times K\n\\]\n\n\\[\n24 = 2K\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( K \\), we find:\n\n\\[\nK = 12\n\\]\n\nNext, we must ensure that the constant terms do not satisfy the same ratio, which would make the lines coincident. The condition for the lines to be parallel but not coincident is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a}{b} = \\frac{a'}{b'} \\neq \\frac{c}{c'}\n\\]\n\nWe have already established that \\(\\frac{a}{b} = \\frac{a'}{b'}\\). Now, check the constant terms:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{7}{7} = 1\n\\]\n\nSince \\(\\frac{3}{2} \\neq 1\\), the lines are indeed parallel and not coincident, confirming that the system has no solutions when \\( K = 12 \\).\n\nThus, the value of \\( K \\) is \\(\\boxed{12}\\)."

We want to find out how many calories, denoted as \\( x \\), are in a 12 fluid ounce bottle. The proportion can be set up as follows:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{125 \\text{ calories}}{8 \\text{ fluid ounces}} = \\frac{x \\text{ calories}}{12 \\text{ fluid ounces}}\n\\]\n\nTo solve for \\( x \\), we cross-multiply:\n\n\\[\n125 \\times 12 = 8 \\times x\n\\]\n\n\\[\n1500 = 8x\n\\]\n\nNow, divide both sides by 8 to solve for \\( x \\):\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{1500}{8} = 187.5\n\\]\n\nTherefore, a 12 fluid ounce bottle of Vitamin Water contains 187.5 calories. The answer is 187.5.'
"To simplify the expression \\(\\root 3 \\of {x \\root 3 \\of {x \\root 3 \\of {x \\sqrt{x}}}}\\), we will work from the innermost radical outward. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Innermost Expression:**\n   \\[\n   x \\sqrt{x} = x \\cdot x^{1/2} = x^{1 + 1/2} = x^{3/2}.\n   \\]\n\n2. **Next Layer:**\n   \\[\n   \\root 3 \\of {x \\sqrt{x}} = \\root 3 \\of {x^{3/2}} = (x^{3/2})^{1/3} = x^{(3/2) \\cdot (1/3)} = x^{1/2}.\n   \\]\n\n3. **Substitute into the Next Layer:**\n   \\[\n   x \\root 3 \\of {x \\sqrt{x}} = x \\cdot x^{1/2} = x^{1 + 1/2} = x^{3/2}.\n   \\]\n\n4. **Next Layer:**\n   \\[\n   \\root 3 \\of {x \\root 3 \\of {x \\sqrt{x}}} = \\root 3 \\of {x^{3/2}} = (x^{3/2})^{1/3} = x^{(3/2) \\cdot (1/3)} = x^{1/2}.\n   \\]\n\n5. **Substitute into the Outermost Layer:**\n   \\[\n   x \\root 3 \\of {x \\root 3 \\of {x \\sqrt{x}}} = x \\cdot x^{1/2} = x^{1 + 1/2} = x^{3/2}.\n   \\]\n\n6. **Final Expression:**\n   \\[\n   \\root 3 \\of {x \\root 3 \\of {x \\root 3 \\of {x \\sqrt{x}}}} = \\root 3 \\of {x^{3/2}} = (x^{3/2})^{1/3} = x^{(3/2) \\cdot (1/3)} = x^{1/2}.\n   \\]\n\nThus, the simplified form of the original expression is \\(\\boxed{x^{1/2}}\\)."
"To solve this problem, we need to determine the cost per extra hour charged by the Internet service provider.\n\nLet's denote:\n- \\( F \\) as the number of free hours each person gets.\n- \\( C \\) as the cost in cents for each additional hour beyond the free hours.\n\nFrom the problem, we have the following information:\n1. Wells and Ted together used 105 hours and paid a total of $10 (or 1000 cents).\n2. Vino used 105 hours by himself and paid $26 (or 2600 cents).\n\nSince Wells and Ted together used 105 hours and paid 1000 cents, and each used all their free hours, the total number of extra hours they used is \\( 105 - 2F \\) (since both used their free hours).\n\nThe equation for Wells and Ted is:\n\\[ C \\times (105 - 2F) = 1000 \\]\n\nFor Vino, who used 105 hours and paid 2600 cents, the number of extra hours he used is \\( 105 - F \\).\n\nThe equation for Vino is:\n\\[ C \\times (105 - F) = 2600 \\]\n\nNow, we have two equations:\n1. \\( C \\times (105 - 2F) = 1000 \\)\n2. \\( C \\times (105 - F) = 2600 \\)\n\nWe can solve these equations simultaneously. First, divide the second equation by the first to eliminate \\( C \\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{C \\times (105 - F)}{C \\times (105 - 2F)} = \\frac{2600}{1000}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we get:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{105 - F}{105 - 2F} = \\frac{26}{10} = \\frac{13}{5}\n\\]\n\nCross-multiplying gives:\n\n\\[\n5(105 - F) = 13(105 - 2F)\n\\]\n\nExpanding both sides:\n\n\\[\n525 - 5F = 1365 - 26F\n\\]\n\nRearranging terms:\n\n\\[\n21F = 840\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( F \\):\n\n\\[\nF = 40\n\\]\n\nNow that we know \\( F = 40 \\), substitute back into one of the original equations to find \\( C \\). Using the first equation:\n\n\\[\nC \\times (105 - 2 \\times 40) = 1000\n\\]\n\n\\[\nC \\times 25 = 1000\n\\]\n\n\\[\nC = \\frac{1000}{25} = 40\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the cost per extra hour is 40 cents. The answer is \\(\\boxed{40}\\) cents per extra hour."
"To find the value of \\(\\frac{a}{d}\\), we need to use the given ratios and express \\(\\frac{a}{d}\\) in terms of these ratios. We are given:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a}{b} = \\frac{3}{5}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\frac{b}{c} = \\frac{15}{6} = \\frac{5}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\frac{c}{d} = 6\n\\]\n\nWe want to find \\(\\frac{a}{d}\\). We can do this by multiplying the given ratios together:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a}{d} = \\frac{a}{b} \\times \\frac{b}{c} \\times \\frac{c}{d}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute the given values:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a}{d} = \\frac{3}{5} \\times \\frac{5}{2} \\times 6\n\\]\n\nNow, let's simplify step by step:\n\n1. Start by comparing the given quadratic \\( x^2 + 25x + c \\) with the expanded form of the binomial square \\( x^2 + 2ax + a^2 \\).\n\n2. From the comparison, we see that the coefficient of \\( x \\) in both expressions must be equal. Therefore, we have:\n   \\[\n   2a = 25\n   \\]\n\n3. Solve for \\( a \\):\n   \\[\n   a = \\frac{25}{2}\n   \\]\n\n4. The constant term \\( c \\) in the expression \\( x^2 + 25x + c \\) must equal \\( a^2 \\). Therefore, the value of \\( c \\) is:\n   \\[\n   c = \\frac{625}{4}\n   \\]\n\nThus, the value of the constant \\( c \\) is \\( \\frac{625}{4} \\).'
'To find the shortest distance between the two circles given by the equations \\((x-9)^2 + (y-5)^2 = 6.25\\) and \\((x+6)^2 + (y+3)^2 = 49\\), we need to follow these steps:\n\n1. **Identify the centers and radii of the circles:**\n\n   - The first circle \\((x-9)^2 + (y-5)^2 = 6.25\\) has its center at \\((9, 5)\\) and a radius of \\(\\sqrt{6.25} = 2.5\\).\n\n   - The second circle \\((x+6)^2 + (y+3)^2 = 49\\) has its center at \\((-6, -3)\\) and a radius of \\(\\sqrt{49} = 7\\).\n\n2. **Calculate the distance between the centers of the circles:**\n\n   The distance \\(d\\) between the centers \\((9, 5)\\) and \\((-6, -3)\\) is given by the distance formula:\n\n   \\[\n   d = \\sqrt{(9 - (-6))^2 + (5 - (-3))^2} = \\sqrt{(9 + 6)^2 + (5 + 3)^2} = \\sqrt{15^2 + 8^2} = \\sqrt{225 + 64} = \\sqrt{289} = 17\n   \\]\n\n3. **Determine the shortest distance between the circles:**\n\n   The shortest distance between the two circles is the distance between their centers minus the sum of their radii. This is because the shortest path between two circles is along the line connecting their centers, minus the radii at each end.\n\n   The sum of the radii is \\(2.5 + 7 = 9.5\\).\n\n   Therefore, the shortest distance between the circles is:\n\n   \\[\n   17 - 9.5 = 7.5\n   \\]\n\nThus, the shortest distance between the two circles is \\(7.5\\) units.'
'To solve the expression \\((4^3 + 2^3) - (3^3 + 1^3)\\), we will follow the steps outlined in the hint:\n\n1. Calculate \\(4^3\\):\n   \\[\n   4^3 = 4 \\times 4 \\times 4 = 64\n   \\]\n\n2. Calculate \\(2^3\\):\n   \\[\n   2^3 = 2 \\times 2 \\times 2 = 8\n   \\]\n\n3. Calculate \\(3^3\\):\n   \\[\n   3^3 = 3 \\times 3 \\times 3 = 27\n   \\]\n\n4. Calculate \\(1^3\\):\n   \\[\n   1^3 = 1 \\times 1 \\times 1 = 1\n   \\]\n\n5. Add the results of \\(4^3\\) and \\(2^3\\):\n   \\[\n   64 + 8 = 72\n   \\]\n\n6. Add the results of \\(3^3\\) and \\(1^3\\):\n   \\[\n   27 + 1 = 28\n   \\]\n\n7. Subtract the sum of \\(3^3 + 1^3\\) from the sum of \\(4^3 + 2^3\\):\n   \\[\n   72 - 28 = 44\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\((4^3 + 2^3) - (3^3 + 1^3)\\) is \\(\\boxed{44}\\).'
'To solve for \\( x^3 - y^3 \\) given the equations \\( x - y = 1 \\) and \\( x^2 + y^2 = 7 \\), we can use the identity for the difference of cubes:\n\n\\[\nx^3 - y^3 = (x-y)(x^2 + xy + y^2)\n\\]\n\nWe already know \\( x - y = 1 \\). To find \\( x^2 + xy + y^2 \\), we can use the identity for the square of a sum:\n\n\\[\n(x+y)^2 = x^2 + 2xy + y^2\n\\]\n\nWe also have:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + y^2 = 7\n\\]\n\nFrom the equation \\( x - y = 1 \\), we can express \\( x \\) in terms of \\( y \\) as \\( x = y + 1 \\). Substitute this into the equation for \\( x^2 + y^2 \\):\n\n\\[\n(y+1)^2 + y^2 = 7\n\\]\n\nExpanding \\( (y+1)^2 \\), we get:\n\n\\[\ny^2 + 2y + 1 + y^2 = 7\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we have:\n\n\\[\n2y^2 + 2y + 1 = 7\n\\]\n\nSubtract 1 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n2y^2 + 2y = 6\n\\]\n\nDivide the entire equation by 2:\n\n\\[\ny^2 + y = 3\n\\]\n\nNow, we can find \\( xy \\) using the identity:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + y^2 = (x-y)^2 + 2xy\n\\]\n\nSubstitute the known values:\n\n\\[\n7 = 1^2 + 2xy\n\\]\n\n\\[\n7 = 1 + 2xy\n\\]\n\nSubtract 1 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n6 = 2xy\n\\]\n\nDivide by 2:\n\n\\[\nxy = 3\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute back to find \\( x^2 + xy + y^2 \\):\n\n\\[\nx^2 + xy + y^2 = 7 + 3 = 10\n\\]\n\nFinally, substitute into the expression for \\( x^3 - y^3 \\):\n\n\\[\nx^3 - y^3 = (x-y)(x^2 + xy + y^2) = 1 \\times 10 = 10\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( x^3 - y^3 \\) is \\(\\boxed{10}\\).'
"To solve the problem, we need to find the positive value of \\( x \\) such that \\( x \\cdot \\lfloor x \\rfloor = 27 \\). Here, \\(\\lfloor x \\rfloor\\) represents the greatest integer less than or equal to \\( x \\).\n\nLet's denote \\(\\lfloor x \\rfloor = n\\), where \\( n \\) is an integer. This implies that \\( n \\leq x < n+1 \\).\n\nGiven the equation:\n\\[ \nx \\cdot n = 27 \n\\]\nwe can express \\( x \\) as:\n\\[ \nx = \\frac{27}{n} \n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\( x = \\frac{27}{n} \\) into the inequality \\( n \\leq x < n+1 \\), we have:\n\\[ \nn \\leq \\frac{27}{n} < n+1 \n\\]\n\nLet's solve these inequalities separately:\n\n1. **Solve \\( n \\leq \\frac{27}{n} \\):**\n\n   Multiply both sides by \\( n \\) (assuming \\( n > 0 \\)):\n   \\[\n   n^2 \\leq 27\n   \\]\n   Taking the square root of both sides:\n   \\[\n   n \\leq \\sqrt{27} \\approx 5.196\n   \\]\n   Since \\( n \\) is an integer, \\( n \\leq 5 \\).\n\n2. **Solve \\( \\frac{27}{n} < n+1 \\):**\n\n   Multiply both sides by \\( n \\):\n   \\[\n   27 < n(n+1)\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   n^2 + n > 27\n   \\]\n\n   To find the range of \\( n \\), solve the quadratic equation \\( n^2 + n - 27 = 0 \\) using the quadratic formula:\n   \\[\n   n = \\frac{-1 \\pm \\sqrt{1 + 4 \\times 27}}{2} = \\frac{-1 \\pm \\sqrt{109}}{2}\n   \\]\n\n   Approximating the roots:\n   \\[\n   n \\approx \\frac{-1 \\pm 10.4403}{2}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   n \\approx 4.72015 \\quad \\text{or} \\quad n \\approx -5.72015\n   \\]\n\n   Since \\( n \\) must be positive, consider \\( n > 4.72015 \\), so \\( n \\geq 5 \\).\n\nCombining both conditions \\( n \\leq 5 \\) and \\( n \\geq 5 \\), we find \\( n = 5 \\).\n\nSubstitute \\( n = 5 \\) back into \\( x = \\frac{27}{n} \\):\n\\[\nx = \\frac{27}{5} = 5.4\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( x \\) is \\(\\boxed{5.4}\\)."
'To find the least possible value of the sum \\( |x - 1| + |x - 1.5| + |x - 2| \\), we need to consider the nature of absolute values and how they relate to distances on the number line.\n\n1. **Understanding the Expression**: The expression \\( |x - 1| + |x - 1.5| + |x - 2| \\) represents the total distance from a point \\( x \\) to the points 1, 1.5, and 2 on the real number line.\n\n2. **Finding the Minimum**: The minimum value of the sum of absolute values occurs at the median of the points involved. This is because the median minimizes the total distance to all points in a set.\n\n3. **Identifying the Median**: The points we are considering are 1, 1.5, and 2. The median of these three points is 1.5.\n\n4. **Evaluating the Expression at the Median**: We evaluate the expression at \\( x = 1.5 \\):\n   \\[\n   |1.5 - 1| + |1.5 - 1.5| + |1.5 - 2| = 0.5 + 0 + 0.5 = 1\n   \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion**: Therefore, the least possible value of the sum \\( |x - 1| + |x - 1.5| + |x - 2| \\) is 1.\n\nThe answer is 1.'
"Let's denote the following:\n\n- \\( t \\) as the time Mike rode.\n- \\( r \\) as the rate (speed) at which Mike rode.\n- \\( 2t \\) as the time Josh rode (since Josh rode for twice the length of time as Mike).\n- \\( \\frac{4}{5}r \\) as the rate at which Josh rode (since Josh rode at four-fifths of Mike's rate).\n\nThe distance Josh rode can be expressed as:\n\\[ \\text{Distance Josh rode} = \\left(\\frac{4}{5}r\\right) \\times (2t) = \\frac{8}{5}rt. \\]\n\nThe distance Mike rode can be expressed as:\n\\[ \\text{Distance Mike rode} = r \\times t = rt. \\]\n\nSince they met after covering a total distance of 13 miles, we have:\n\\[ \\frac{8}{5}rt + rt = 13. \\]\n\nCombining the terms on the left side:\n\\[ \\frac{8}{5}rt + \\frac{5}{5}rt = \\frac{13}{5}rt = 13. \\]\n\nSolving for \\( rt \\):\n\\[ \\frac{13}{5}rt = 13 \\]\n\\[ rt = 13 \\times \\frac{5}{13} \\]\n\\[ rt = 5. \\]\n\nTherefore, Mike rode 5 miles when they met. The answer is \\(\\boxed{5}\\)."
'To solve for \\( f(f(9)) \\), we need to use the information given about the function \\( g(x) = f^{-1}(x) \\), which implies that \\( f(g(x)) = x \\).\n\nFrom the given values:\n- \\( g(3) = 9 \\) implies \\( f(9) = 3 \\).\n- \\( g(9) = 20 \\) implies \\( f(20) = 9 \\).\n\nWe need to find \\( f(f(9)) \\). From the information above, we know:\n- \\( f(9) = 3 \\).\n\nTherefore, \\( f(f(9)) = f(3) \\).\n\nTo find \\( f(3) \\), we use the inverse relationship:\n- Since \\( g(0) = 3 \\), it follows that \\( f(3) = 0 \\).\n\nThus, \\( f(f(9)) = f(3) = 0 \\).\n\nThe answer is \\(\\boxed{0}\\).'
'To solve the problem of expanding \\((x-2)^2(x+2)^2\\) and finding the product of the nonzero coefficients, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Recognize the Structure**: The expression \\((x-2)^2(x+2)^2\\) can be seen as \\((a^2)(b^2)\\) where \\(a = (x-2)\\) and \\(b = (x+2)\\). Using the identity \\((a^2)(b^2) = (ab)^2\\), we can rewrite it as \\(((x-2)(x+2))^2\\).\n\n2. **Simplify Using Difference of Squares**: The expression \\((x-2)(x+2)\\) is a difference of squares, which simplifies to:\n   \\[\n   x^2 - 4\n   \\]\n\n3. **Square the Result**: Now, we need to expand \\((x^2 - 4)^2\\). This can be done using the binomial theorem:\n   \\[\n   (x^2 - 4)^2 = (x^2)^2 - 2 \\cdot x^2 \\cdot 4 + 4^2\n   \\]\n\n4. **Calculate Each Term**:\n   - \\((x^2)^2 = x^4\\)\n   - \\(-2 \\cdot x^2 \\cdot 4 = -8x^2\\)\n   - \\(4^2 = 16\\)\n\n5. **Combine the Terms**: The expanded form of the expression is:\n   \\[\n   x^4 - 8x^2 + 16\n   \\]\n\n6. **Identify Nonzero Coefficients**: The nonzero coefficients in this expression are:\n   - 1 (for \\(x^4\\))\n   - -8 (for \\(x^2\\))\n   - 16 (the constant term)\n\n7. **Calculate the Product of Nonzero Coefficients**:\n   \\[\n   1 \\times (-8) \\times 16 = -128\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the product of the nonzero coefficients of the resulting expression is \\(-128\\).'
'Let the three consecutive positive even numbers be \\( x - 2 \\), \\( x \\), and \\( x + 2 \\). The sum of their squares is given by:\n\n\\[\n(x-2)^2 + x^2 + (x+2)^2 = 12296\n\\]\n\nExpanding each term, we have:\n\n\\[\n(x-2)^2 = x^2 - 4x + 4\n\\]\n\\[\nx^2 = x^2\n\\]\n\\[\n(x+2)^2 = x^2 + 4x + 4\n\\]\n\nAdding these, the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\n(x^2 - 4x + 4) + x^2 + (x^2 + 4x + 4) = 12296\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we get:\n\n\\[\n3x^2 + 8 = 12296\n\\]\n\nSubtract 8 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n3x^2 = 12288\n\\]\n\nDivide by 3:\n\n\\[\nx^2 = 4096\n\\]\n\nTaking the square root of both sides, we find:\n\n\\[\nx = 64\n\\]\n\nThus, the three consecutive even numbers are \\( 62 \\), \\( 64 \\), and \\( 66 \\).\n\nNext, we find the product of these numbers:\n\n\\[\n62 \\times 64 \\times 66\n\\]\n\nTo simplify the calculation, notice that:\n\n\\[\n62 \\times 66 = (64 - 2)(64 + 2) = 64^2 - 2^2 = 4096 - 4 = 4092\n\\]\n\nNow, multiply by 64:\n\n\\[\n4092 \\times 64\n\\]\n\nUsing the distributive property:\n\n\\[\n4092 \\times 64 = (4092 \\times 60) + (4092 \\times 4)\n\\]\n\nCalculate each part:\n\n\\[\n4092 \\times 60 = 245520\n\\]\n\\[\n4092 \\times 4 = 16368\n\\]\n\nAdd these results:\n\n\\[\n245520 + 16368 = 261888\n\\]\n\nFinally, divide the product by 8:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{261888}{8} = 32736\n\\]\n\nThus, the product of the three numbers divided by 8 is \\(\\boxed{32736}\\).'
'To solve the inequality \\( x^2 + 4x + 4 < 20 \\), we first simplify it:\n\n1. Subtract 20 from both sides to get:\n   \\[\n   x^2 + 4x + 4 - 20 < 0\n   \\]\n   which simplifies to:\n   \\[\n   x^2 + 4x - 16 < 0\n   \\]\n\n2. We need to find the roots of the equation \\( x^2 + 4x - 16 = 0 \\) using the quadratic formula:\n   \\[\n   x = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n   \\]\n   where \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = 4 \\), and \\( c = -16 \\).\n\n3. Calculate the discriminant:\n   \\[\n   b^2 - 4ac = 4^2 - 4 \\times 1 \\times (-16) = 16 + 64 = 80\n   \\]\n\n4. Find the roots:\n   \\[\n   x = \\frac{-4 \\pm \\sqrt{80}}{2} = \\frac{-4 \\pm 4\\sqrt{5}}{2} = -2 \\pm 2\\sqrt{5}\n   \\]\n\n5. Approximate the roots:\n   \\[\n   -2 + 2\\sqrt{5} \\approx 2.472 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad -2 - 2\\sqrt{5} \\approx -6.472\n   \\]\n\n6. The inequality \\( x^2 + 4x - 16 < 0 \\) is satisfied for values of \\( x \\) between the roots \\( -2 - 2\\sqrt{5} \\) and \\( -2 + 2\\sqrt{5} \\). Since we are looking for positive integer values of \\( x \\), we consider the integers between these roots.\n\n7. The positive integer values of \\( x \\) that fall between these roots are \\( 1 \\) and \\( 2 \\).\n\n8. Verify these values:\n   - For \\( x = 1 \\):\n     \\[\n     1^2 + 4 \\times 1 + 4 = 1 + 4 + 4 = 9 < 20\n     \\]\n   - For \\( x = 2 \\):\n     \\[\n     2^2 + 4 \\times 2 + 4 = 4 + 8 + 4 = 16 < 20\n     \\]\n\nBoth values satisfy the inequality. Therefore, there are \\(\\boxed{2}\\) positive integer values of \\( x \\) for which the inequality \\( x^2 + 4x + 4 < 20 \\) is satisfied.'

'To find the minimum possible slope of a line that passes through the point \\((4, 365)\\) and has a \\(y\\)-intercept between 1 and 9, we can use the slope-intercept form of a line, which is \\(y = mx + c\\), where \\(m\\) is the slope and \\(c\\) is the \\(y\\)-intercept.\n\nThe slope \\(m\\) of a line passing through two points \\((x_1, y_1)\\) and \\((x_2, y_2)\\) is given by:\n\n\\[\nm = \\frac{y_2 - y_1}{x_2 - x_1}\n\\]\n\nHere, one point is \\((4, 365)\\) and the other point is \\((0, c)\\), where \\(c\\) is the \\(y\\)-intercept. Therefore, the slope \\(m\\) is:\n\n\\[\nm = \\frac{365 - c}{4 - 0} = \\frac{365 - c}{4}\n\\]\n\nTo find the minimum possible slope, we need to maximize the value of \\(c\\) because the slope is inversely proportional to \\(c\\). The maximum value of \\(c\\) within the given range is 9.\n\nSubstituting \\(c = 9\\) into the slope formula gives:\n\n\\[\nm = \\frac{365 - 9}{4} = \\frac{356}{4} = 89\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the minimum possible slope of the line is \\(\\boxed{89}\\).'
"To solve for \\( x - y \\) given the equations:\n\n1. \\( 725x + 727y = 1500 \\)\n2. \\( 729x + 731y = 1508 \\)\n\nwe start by subtracting the first equation from the second:\n\n\\[\n(729x + 731y) - (725x + 727y) = 1508 - 1500\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we get:\n\n\\[\n(729x - 725x) + (731y - 727y) = 8\n\\]\n\n\\[\n4x + 4y = 8\n\\]\n\nDividing the entire equation by 4:\n\n\\[\nx + y = 2\n\\]\n\nNow, we need to find \\( x - y \\). We already have \\( x + y = 2 \\). Let's express \\( x \\) and \\( y \\) in terms of \\( x - y \\).\n\nLet \\( x - y = a \\). We have the system:\n\n1. \\( x + y = 2 \\)\n2. \\( x - y = a \\)\n\nAdding these two equations:\n\n\\[\n(x + y) + (x - y) = 2 + a\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2x = 2 + a\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = 1 + \\frac{a}{2}\n\\]\n\nSubtracting the second equation from the first:\n\n\\[\n(x + y) - (x - y) = 2 - a\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2y = 2 - a\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = 1 - \\frac{a}{2}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\( x = 1 + \\frac{a}{2} \\) and \\( y = 1 - \\frac{a}{2} \\) back into one of the original equations to solve for \\( a \\). Using the first equation:\n\n\\[\n725\\left(1 + \\frac{a}{2}\\right) + 727\\left(1 - \\frac{a}{2}\\right) = 1500\n\\]\n\nExpanding both terms:\n\n\\[\n725 + \\frac{725a}{2} + 727 - \\frac{727a}{2} = 1500\n\\]\n\nCombine like terms:\n\n\\[\n1452 + \\frac{725a}{2} - \\frac{727a}{2} = 1500\n\\]\n\n\\[\n1452 + \\frac{-2a}{2} = 1500\n\\]\n\n\\[\n1452 - a = 1500\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( a \\):\n\n\\[\n-a = 1500 - 1452\n\\]\n\n\\[\n-a = 48\n\\]\n\n\\[\na = -48\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( x - y \\) is \\(\\boxed{-48}\\)."

Therefore, \\(8\\sqrt{2} = 2^3 \\cdot 2^{1/2}\\).\n\n3. 'Given that \\( f \\) is an invertible function and satisfies the condition \\( f(f(x)) = x \\), we can deduce some important properties about \\( f \\).\n\n1. **Understanding the condition \\( f(f(x)) = x \\):**\n   - This condition implies that applying the function \\( f \\) twice returns the original input \\( x \\). \n   - This is a characteristic of an involution, which means that \\( f \\) is its own inverse. In other words, \\( f = f^{-1} \\).\n\n2. **Finding \\( f(x) - f^{-1}(x) \\):**\n   - Since \\( f = f^{-1} \\), it follows that for any \\( x \\), \\( f(x) = f^{-1}(x) \\).\n   - Therefore, the expression \\( f(x) - f^{-1}(x) \\) simplifies to:\n     \\[\n     f(x) - f^{-1}(x) = f(x) - f(x) = 0\n     \\]\n\nThus, the expression for \\( f(x) - f^{-1}(x) \\) is \\(\\boxed{0}\\).'
'To find the simplified value of \\(\\frac{7}{30} @ \\frac{10}{21}\\) using the operation defined as \\(\\frac{m}{n} @ \\frac{p}{q} = (m)(p)\\left(\\frac{q}{n}\\right)\\), we follow these steps:\n\n1. Identify the values: \\(m = 7\\), \\(n = 30\\), \\(p = 10\\), and \\(q = 21\\).\n\n2. Substitute these values into the operation:\n   \\[\n   (7)(10)\\left(\\frac{21}{30}\\right)\n   \\]\n\n3. Calculate \\(7 \\times 10\\):\n   \\[\n   7 \\times 10 = 70\n   \\]\n\n4. Simplify \\(\\frac{21}{30}\\):\n   - The greatest common divisor (GCD) of 21 and 30 is 3.\n   - Divide both the numerator and the denominator by 3:\n     \\[\n     \\frac{21}{30} = \\frac{21 \\div 3}{30 \\div 3} = \\frac{7}{10}\n     \\]\n\n5. Substitute the simplified fraction back into the expression:\n   \\[\n   70 \\times \\frac{7}{10}\n   \\]\n\n6. Calculate the product:\n   - Multiply 70 by \\(\\frac{7}{10}\\):\n     \\[\n     70 \\times \\frac{7}{10} = \\frac{70 \\times 7}{10} = \\frac{490}{10}\n     \\]\n\n7. Simplify \\(\\frac{490}{10}\\):\n   - Divide the numerator by the denominator:\n     \\[\n     \\frac{490}{10} = 49\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, the simplified value of \\(\\frac{7}{30} @ \\frac{10}{21}\\) is \\(\\boxed{49}\\).'
'To evaluate \\(\\log_{\\sqrt{5}} 125\\sqrt{5}\\), we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Express the Argument in Terms of Powers of 5:**\n   - The argument is \\(125\\sqrt{5}\\).\n   - We know that \\(125 = 5^3\\).\n   - Therefore, \\(125\\sqrt{5} = 5^3 \\times 5^{1/2} = 5^{3 + 1/2} = 5^{7/2}\\).\n\n2. **Use the Logarithmic Identity:**\n   - We have \\(\\log_{\\sqrt{5}} 5^{7/2}\\).\n   - Using the identity \\(\\log_b a^c = c \\log_b a\\), we can write:\n     \\[\n     \\log_{\\sqrt{5}} 5^{7/2} = \\frac{7}{2} \\log_{\\sqrt{5}} 5\n     \\]\n\n3. **Evaluate \\(\\log_{\\sqrt{5}} 5\\):**\n   - The base \\(\\sqrt{5}\\) can be expressed as \\(5^{1/2}\\).\n   - Therefore, \\(\\log_{\\sqrt{5}} 5 = \\log_{5^{1/2}} 5\\).\n   - Using the change of base formula, \\(\\log_{5^{1/2}} 5 = \\frac{\\log_5 5}{\\log_5 5^{1/2}}\\).\n   - We know \\(\\log_5 5 = 1\\) and \\(\\log_5 5^{1/2} = \\frac{1}{2}\\).\n   - Thus, \\(\\log_{5^{1/2}} 5 = \\frac{1}{1/2} = 2\\).\n\n4. **Calculate the Final Result:**\n   - Substitute back into the expression:\n     \\[\n     \\log_{\\sqrt{5}} 5^{7/2} = \\frac{7}{2} \\times 2 = 7\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\(\\log_{\\sqrt{5}} 125\\sqrt{5}\\) is \\(\\boxed{7}\\).'
'To find the numerical value of the expression \\((b-c)^2 + a(b+c)\\) when \\(a = 2\\), \\(b = 3\\), and \\(c = 4\\), we follow these steps:\n\n1. Substitute the given values into the expression: \n   \\[\n   (3-4)^2 + 2(3+4)\n   \\]\n\n2. Calculate \\((3-4)^2\\):\n   \\[\n   (3-4)^2 = (-1)^2 = 1\n   \\]\n\n3. Calculate \\(2(3+4)\\):\n   \\[\n   2(3+4) = 2 \\times 7 = 14\n   \\]\n\n4. Add the results from steps 2 and 3:\n   \\[\n   1 + 14 = 15\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the numerical value of the expression is \\(\\boxed{15}\\).'
'In an arithmetic sequence, each term is given by \\(a_n = a_1 + (n-1)d\\), where \\(a_1\\) is the first term and \\(d\\) is the common difference.\n\nGiven that \\(\\frac{a_4}{a_2} = 3\\), we can express \\(a_4\\) and \\(a_2\\) in terms of \\(a_1\\) and \\(d\\):\n\n\\[\na_4 = a_1 + 3d\n\\]\n\\[\na_2 = a_1 + d\n\\]\n\nSubstituting these into the given ratio:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a_4}{a_2} = \\frac{a_1 + 3d}{a_1 + d} = 3\n\\]\n\nCross-multiplying gives:\n\n\\[\na_1 + 3d = 3(a_1 + d)\n\\]\n\nExpanding the right side:\n\n\\[\na_1 + 3d = 3a_1 + 3d\n\\]\n\nSubtracting \\(3d\\) from both sides:\n\n\\[\na_1 = 3a_1\n\\]\n\nSubtracting \\(a_1\\) from both sides:\n\n\\[\n0 = 2a_1\n\\]\n\nThus, \\(a_1 = 0\\).\n\nNow, we need to find \\(\\frac{a_5}{a_3}\\):\n\n\\[\na_5 = a_1 + 4d = 0 + 4d = 4d\n\\]\n\\[\na_3 = a_1 + 2d = 0 + 2d = 2d\n\\]\n\nSo, the ratio is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a_5}{a_3} = \\frac{4d}{2d} = 2\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\(\\frac{a_5}{a_3}\\) is \\(\\boxed{2}\\).'
'The function \\( f(x) = \\left(\\frac{3}{7}\\right)^x \\) is an exponential function with a base of \\(\\frac{3}{7}\\), which is a positive number less than 1. This means that as \\( x \\) increases, the value of \\(\\left(\\frac{3}{7}\\right)^x\\) decreases.\n\n1. At \\( x = 0 \\), \\( f(0) = \\left(\\frac{3}{7}\\right)^0 = 1 \\).\n2. As \\( x \\) approaches infinity, \\(\\left(\\frac{3}{7}\\right)^x\\) approaches 0 because the base is less than 1.\n\nTherefore, the function starts at 1 when \\( x = 0 \\) and decreases towards 0 as \\( x \\) increases. However, it never actually reaches 0, only approaches it asymptotically.\n\nThus, the range of the function is all positive real numbers less than or equal to 1. In interval notation, this is expressed as \\( (0, 1] \\).\n\nThe answer is that the range of the function \\( f(x) = \\left(\\frac{3}{7}\\right)^x \\) is \\( (0, 1] \\).'
"To find the sum of the areas of all the circles, we first need to determine the area of each circle and then sum these areas.\n\n1. **Determine the radii of the circles:**\n   - The diameters of the circles are 16 inches, 8 inches, 4 inches, and so on.\n   - The radii of the circles are half of their diameters: 8 inches, 4 inches, 2 inches, and so on.\n\n2. **Calculate the area of each circle:**\n   - The formula for the area of a circle is \\( A = \\pi r^2 \\).\n   - For the first circle with a radius of 8 inches, the area is \\( \\pi \\times 8^2 = 64\\pi \\).\n   - For the second circle with a radius of 4 inches, the area is \\( \\pi \\times 4^2 = 16\\pi \\).\n   - For the third circle with a radius of 2 inches, the area is \\( \\pi \\times 2^2 = 4\\pi \\).\n   - This pattern continues with each subsequent circle having an area that is one-fourth of the previous circle's area.\n\n3. **Sum the areas of all circles:**\n   - The areas form a geometric series: \\( 64\\pi, 16\\pi, 4\\pi, \\ldots \\).\n   - The first term \\( a = 64\\pi \\) and the common ratio \\( r = \\frac{1}{4} \\).\n\n4. **Use the formula for the sum of an infinite geometric series:**\n   - The sum \\( S \\) of an infinite geometric series with first term \\( a \\) and common ratio \\( r \\) (where \\( |r| < 1 \\)) is given by:\n     \\[\n     S = \\frac{a}{1 - r}\n     \\]\n   - Substituting the values, we get:\n     \\[\n     S = \\frac{64\\pi}{1 - \\frac{1}{4}} = \\frac{64\\pi}{\\frac{3}{4}} = \\frac{64\\pi \\times 4}{3} = \\frac{256\\pi}{3}\n     \\]\n\n5. **Calculate the numerical value and round to the nearest whole number:**\n   - Using \\( \\pi \\approx 3.14159 \\), we find:\n     \\[\n     S \\approx \\frac{256 \\times 3.14159}{3} \\approx 267.946\n     \\]\n   - Rounding to the nearest whole number, the sum of the areas is approximately \\( \\boxed{268} \\) square inches."
'To find the difference between the sum of the first 2003 even counting numbers and the sum of the first 2003 odd counting numbers, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Sum of Even Counting Numbers**: The first 2003 even numbers are 2, 4, 6, ..., 4006. These numbers can be expressed as \\(2n\\), where \\(n\\) ranges from 1 to 2003. The sum of these numbers is given by the formula for the sum of an arithmetic series:\n\n   \\[\n   S_{\\text{even}} = 2(1 + 2 + 3 + \\ldots + 2003) = 2 \\times \\frac{2003 \\times 2004}{2} = 2003 \\times 2004\n   \\]\n\n2. **Sum of Odd Counting Numbers**: The first 2003 odd numbers are 1, 3, 5, ..., 4005. These numbers can be expressed as \\(2n - 1\\), where \\(n\\) ranges from 1 to 2003. The sum of these numbers is also given by the formula for the sum of an arithmetic series:\n\n   \\[\n   S_{\\text{odd}} = 1 + 3 + 5 + \\ldots + 4005 = \\frac{2003 \\times 4006}{2} = 2003^2\n   \\]\n\n3. **Difference Between Sums**: The difference between the sum of the first 2003 even numbers and the sum of the first 2003 odd numbers is:\n\n   \\[\n   S_{\\text{even}} - S_{\\text{odd}} = (2003 \\times 2004) - 2003^2\n   \\]\n\n   Simplifying this expression:\n\n   \\[\n   S_{\\text{even}} - S_{\\text{odd}} = 2003 \\times (2004 - 2003) = 2003 \\times 1 = 2003\n   \\]\n\n4. **Final Result**: The difference is 2003.\n\nTherefore, the difference between the sum of the first 2003 even counting numbers and the sum of the first 2003 odd counting numbers is \\(\\boxed{2003}\\).'
'To evaluate \\(\\log_{\\sqrt{8}}(64\\sqrt{8})\\), we need to express both the base \\(\\sqrt{8}\\) and the argument \\(64\\sqrt{8}\\) in terms of powers of the same base, preferably a prime number.\n\nFirst, express \\(\\sqrt{8}\\) in terms of powers of 2:\n\\[\n\\sqrt{8} = 8^{1/2} = (2^3)^{1/2} = 2^{3/2}.\n\\]\n\nNext, express \\(64\\sqrt{8}\\) in terms of powers of 2:\n\\[\n64 = 2^6,\n\\]\nso\n\\[\n64\\sqrt{8} = 64 \\times \\sqrt{8} = 2^6 \\times 2^{3/2} = 2^{6 + 3/2} = 2^{12/2 + 3/2} = 2^{15/2}.\n\\]\n\nNow, we have:\n\\[\n\\log_{\\sqrt{8}}(64\\sqrt{8}) = \\log_{2^{3/2}}(2^{15/2}).\n\\]\n\nUsing the change of base formula for logarithms, we have:\n\\[\n\\log_{2^{3/2}}(2^{15/2}) = \\frac{\\log_2(2^{15/2})}{\\log_2(2^{3/2})}.\n\\]\n\nSimplify each logarithm:\n\\[\n\\log_2(2^{15/2}) = \\frac{15}{2},\n\\]\n\\[\n\\log_2(2^{3/2}) = \\frac{3}{2}.\n\\]\n\nThus, the expression becomes:\n\\[\n\\frac{\\log_2(2^{15/2})}{\\log_2(2^{3/2})} = \\frac{15/2}{3/2} = \\frac{15}{2} \\times \\frac{2}{3} = \\frac{15 \\times 2}{2 \\times 3} = \\frac{15}{3} = 5.\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\(\\log_{\\sqrt{8}}(64\\sqrt{8})\\) is \\(\\boxed{5}\\).'
'Since \\( c \\) and \\( d \\) are inversely proportional, we have the relationship \\( c \\times d = k \\), where \\( k \\) is a constant.\n\nFrom the given information, when \\( c = 9 \\), \\( d = 8 \\). Therefore, we can find the constant \\( k \\) as follows:\n\n\\[\n9 \\times 8 = k \\implies k = 72\n\\]\n\nNow, we need to find the value of \\( d \\) when \\( c = 6 \\). Using the relationship \\( c \\times d = k \\), we substitute \\( c = 6 \\) and \\( k = 72 \\):\n\n\\[\n6 \\times d = 72\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( d \\), we divide both sides by 6:\n\n\\[\nd = \\frac{72}{6} = 12\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( d \\) when \\( c = 6 \\) is \\(\\boxed{12}\\).'
'To find the integer value of \\( x \\) in the arithmetic sequence \\( 9, x, 81 \\), we need to determine the common difference \\( d \\) of the sequence.\n\n1. The first term of the sequence is \\( 9 \\) (which is \\( 3^2 \\)).\n2. The third term of the sequence is \\( 81 \\) (which is \\( 3^4 \\)).\n\nIn an arithmetic sequence, the common difference \\( d \\) is constant between consecutive terms. We can calculate \\( d \\) using the formula:\n\n\\[\nd = \\frac{\\text{third term} - \\text{first term}}{2}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the given values:\n\n\\[\nd = \\frac{81 - 9}{2} = \\frac{72}{2} = 36\n\\]\n\nNow that we have the common difference \\( d = 36 \\), we can find the second term \\( x \\) by adding the common difference to the first term:\n\n\\[\nx = 9 + 36 = 45\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the integer value of \\( x \\) in the arithmetic sequence is \\(\\boxed{45}\\).'
"According to Heisenberg's Uncertainty Principle, the product of the error in the measurement of a particle's momentum (\\(\\Delta p\\)) and the error in the measurement of a particle's position (\\(\\Delta x\\)) must satisfy the inequality:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta x \\cdot \\Delta p \\geq \\frac{\\hbar}{2}\n\\]\n\nwhere \\(\\hbar\\) is the reduced Planck's constant.\n\nIf the error in the measurement of the momentum is halved, the new error in momentum becomes \\(\\frac{\\Delta p}{2}\\). To maintain the inequality, the new error in the measurement of position (\\(\\Delta x'\\)) must satisfy:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta x' \\cdot \\frac{\\Delta p}{2} \\geq \\frac{\\hbar}{2}\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\(\\Delta x'\\), we have:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta x' \\geq \\frac{\\hbar}{2} \\cdot \\frac{2}{\\Delta p} = \\frac{\\hbar}{\\Delta p} = 2 \\Delta x\n\\]\n\nThis means that the new minimum error in the measurement of position (\\(\\Delta x'\\)) is twice the original error (\\(\\Delta x\\)). Therefore, the minimum error in the measurement of position increases by:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{\\Delta x' - \\Delta x}{\\Delta x} \\times 100\\% = \\frac{2\\Delta x - \\Delta x}{\\Delta x} \\times 100\\% = 100\\%\n\\]\n\nThus, the minimum error in the measurement of a particle's position increases by 100% when the error in the measurement of its momentum is halved."
"To solve the problem, we need to find integer values of \\( x \\) such that \\( |x^2 - 16| \\) is a prime number. This involves considering two cases:\n\n1. **Case 1:** \\( x^2 - 16 = p \\), where \\( p \\) is a prime number.\n   - This implies \\( x^2 = p + 16 \\).\n   - For \\( x^2 \\) to be a perfect square, \\( p + 16 \\) must be a perfect square.\n\n2. **Case 2:** \\( 16 - x^2 = p \\), where \\( p \\) is a prime number.\n   - This implies \\( x^2 = 16 - p \\).\n   - For \\( x^2 \\) to be a perfect square, \\( 16 - p \\) must be a perfect square.\n\nLet's analyze these cases:\n\n### Case 1: \\( x^2 = p + 16 \\)\n- \\( x^2 = 17 \\) (since 17 is prime), but 17 is not a perfect square.\n- \\( x^2 = 19 \\) (since 19 is prime), but 19 is not a perfect square.\n- \\( x^2 = 23 \\) (since 23 is prime), but 23 is not a perfect square.\n- \\( x^2 = 31 \\) (since 31 is prime), but 31 is not a perfect square.\n\nNo perfect squares are found in this case.\n\n### Case 2: \\( x^2 = 16 - p \\)\n- \\( x^2 = 15 \\) (since 1 is not prime), not a perfect square.\n- \\( x^2 = 13 \\) (since 3 is prime), not a perfect square.\n- \\( x^2 = 11 \\) (since 5 is prime), not a perfect square.\n- \\( x^2 = 7 \\) (since 9 is not prime), not a perfect square.\n- \\( x^2 = 3 \\) (since 13 is prime), not a perfect square.\n\nHowever, if we consider \\( x^2 = 15 \\) (since 1 is not prime), we find:\n- \\( x^2 = 15 \\) is not a perfect square.\n\nLet's try smaller values:\n- \\( x^2 = 16 - 3 = 13 \\), not a perfect square.\n- \\( x^2 = 16 - 5 = 11 \\), not a perfect square.\n- \\( x^2 = 16 - 7 = 9 \\), which is a perfect square (\\( x = \\pm 3 \\)).\n\nThus, the integer values of \\( x \\) that satisfy the condition are \\( x = 3 \\) and \\( x = -3 \\).\n\n### Product of the Integer Values\nThe product of these integer values is:\n\\[ 3 \\times (-3) = -9 \\]\n\nTherefore, the product of the two integer values for \\( x \\) for which \\( |x^2 - 16| \\) is a prime number is \\(\\boxed{-9}\\)."

'To find the distance between the vertex of the parabola given by the equation \\( y = x^2 + 2x - 6 \\) and the point \\( (4, 5) \\), we first need to determine the vertex of the parabola.\n\n1. **Identify the coefficients**: The given equation is \\( y = x^2 + 2x - 6 \\), where \\( a = 1 \\) and \\( b = 2 \\).\n\n2. **Find the x-coordinate of the vertex**: The formula for the x-coordinate of the vertex of a parabola in the form \\( y = ax^2 + bx + c \\) is \\( x = -\\frac{b}{2a} \\).\n   \\[\n   x = -\\frac{2}{2 \\times 1} = -1\n   \\]\n\n3. **Find the y-coordinate of the vertex**: Substitute \\( x = -1 \\) back into the equation to find the y-coordinate.\n   \\[\n   y = (-1)^2 + 2(-1) - 6 = 1 - 2 - 6 = -7\n   \\]\n\n4. **Vertex of the parabola**: The vertex is \\((-1, -7)\\).\n\n5. **Calculate the distance**: Use the distance formula to find the distance between the vertex \\((-1, -7)\\) and the point \\((4, 5)\\).\n   \\[\n   \\text{Distance} = \\sqrt{(4 - (-1))^2 + (5 - (-7))^2} = \\sqrt{(4 + 1)^2 + (5 + 7)^2} = \\sqrt{5^2 + 12^2} = \\sqrt{25 + 144} = \\sqrt{169} = 13\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the distance between the vertex of the parabola and the point \\((4, 5)\\) is \\( \\boxed{13} \\).'

According to the function definition, for rational \\( x \\), \\( f(x) = |\\lfloor{x}\\rfloor| \\).\n\n   \\(\\lfloor{-2}\\rfloor = -2\\), so \\( f(-2) = |-2| = 2\\).\n\n2. **Evaluate \\( f(-\\pi) \\):**\n\n   \\(-\\pi\\) is an irrational number. For irrational \\( x \\), \\( f(x) = \\lceil{x}\\rceil^2 \\).\n\n   The ceiling of \\(-\\pi\\) is \\(-3\\) because \\(-3\\) is the smallest integer greater than \\(-\\pi\\).\n\n   Therefore, \\( f(-\\pi) = (-3)^2 = 9\\).\n\n3. **Evaluate \\( f(\\sqrt{50}) \\):**\n\n   \\(\\sqrt{50}\\) is irrational. 'To solve the inequality \\((x-4)^2 \\le 9\\), we start by considering the expression \\((x-4)^2\\). This represents the square of the distance between \\(x\\) and 4 on the number line. The inequality \\((x-4)^2 \\le 9\\) implies that this distance is at most 3, since the square root of 9 is 3.\n\nWe can rewrite the inequality as:\n\\[\n-3 \\le x-4 \\le 3\n\\]\n\nThis compound inequality can be split into two separate inequalities:\n1. \\(x - 4 \\ge -3\\)\n2. \\(x - 4 \\le 3\\)\n\nSolving these inequalities separately, we get:\n1. \\(x \\ge -3 + 4\\) which simplifies to \\(x \\ge 1\\)\n2. \\(x \\le 3 + 4\\) which simplifies to \\(x \\le 7\\)\n\nCombining these results, we find that the values of \\(x\\) that satisfy the inequality are those in the range:\n\\[\n1 \\le x \\le 7\n\\]\n\nThe segment on the number line that corresponds to this range is from \\(x = 1\\) to \\(x = 7\\). The length of this segment is the difference between the endpoints:\n\\[\n7 - 1 = 6\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the length of the segment of the number line consisting of the points that satisfy \\((x-4)^2 \\le 9\\) is \\(\\boxed{6}\\).'
"To find the function \\( k(x) \\) such that \\( f(x) \\) is its own inverse, we need to ensure that \\( f(f(x)) = x \\) for all \\( x \\).\n\n### Case 1: \\( x > 0 \\)\n\nFor \\( x > 0 \\), \\( f(x) = k(x) \\). We need \\( f(k(x)) = x \\).\n\nSince \\( k(x) > 0 \\) (because \\( x > 0 \\)), we have:\n\\[ f(k(x)) = k(k(x)) = x. \\]\n\nThis implies that \\( k(x) \\) must be its own inverse for positive \\( x \\). A common function that is its own inverse is the reciprocal function, so we try:\n\\[ k(x) = \\frac{1}{x}. \\]\n\nLet's verify:\n\\[ f(k(x)) = f\\left(\\frac{1}{x}\\right) = k\\left(\\frac{1}{x}\\right) = x. \\]\n\nThis satisfies the condition for \\( x > 0 \\).\n\n### Case 2: \\( x < 0 \\)\n\nFor \\( x < 0 \\), \\( f(x) = -\\frac{1}{2x} \\). We need \\( f\\left(-\\frac{1}{2x}\\right) = x \\).\n\nCalculate:\n\\[ f\\left(-\\frac{1}{2x}\\right) = -\\frac{1}{2\\left(-\\frac{1}{2x}\\right)} = -\\frac{1}{-\\frac{1}{x}} = x. \\]\n\nThis condition is satisfied for \\( x < 0 \\).\n\n### Case 3: \\( x = 0 \\)\n\nFor \\( x = 0 \\), \\( f(x) = 0 \\). We need \\( f(0) = 0 \\), which is already given by the definition of \\( f(x) \\).\n\n### Conclusion\n\nThe function \\( k(x) = \\frac{1}{x} \\) satisfies all the conditions for \\( f(x) \\) to be its own inverse. Therefore, the function \\( k(x) \\) is:\n\n\\[ k(x) = \\frac{1}{x} \\]\n\nfor \\( x > 0 \\)."

'To solve the inequality \\( b^2 + 2b - 15 \\le 0 \\), we first factor the quadratic expression. The expression can be factored as:\n\n\\[\nb^2 + 2b - 15 = (b - 3)(b + 5)\n\\]\n\nThe roots of the equation \\( b^2 + 2b - 15 = 0 \\) are found by setting each factor equal to zero:\n\n1. \\( b - 3 = 0 \\) gives \\( b = 3 \\)\n2. \\( b + 5 = 0 \\) gives \\( b = -5 \\)\n\nThese roots, \\( b = -5 \\) and \\( b = 3 \\), are the critical points that divide the number line into intervals. We need to determine where the product \\( (b - 3)(b + 5) \\) is non-positive (i.e., less than or equal to zero).\n\nThe intervals to test are:\n- \\( (-\\infty, -5) \\)\n- \\([-5, 3]\\)\n- \\( (3, \\infty) \\)\n\nWe test each interval:\n\n1. **Interval \\( (-\\infty, -5) \\):** Choose a test point, such as \\( b = -6 \\).\n   \\[\n   (b - 3)(b + 5) = (-6 - 3)(-6 + 5) = (-9)(-1) = 9 > 0\n   \\]\n   The product is positive, so the inequality does not hold in this interval.\n\n2. **Interval \\([-5, 3]\\):** Choose a test point, such as \\( b = 0 \\).\n   \\[\n   (b - 3)(b + 5) = (0 - 3)(0 + 5) = (-3)(5) = -15 \\le 0\n   \\]\n   The product is negative, so the inequality holds in this interval.\n\n3. **Interval \\( (3, \\infty) \\):** Choose a test point, such as \\( b = 4 \\).\n   \\[\n   (b - 3)(b + 5) = (4 - 3)(4 + 5) = (1)(9) = 9 > 0\n   \\]\n   The product is positive, so the inequality does not hold in this interval.\n\nThe inequality \\( (b - 3)(b + 5) \\le 0 \\) holds in the interval \\([-5, 3]\\). Therefore, the least value of \\( b \\) in this interval is \\( b = -5 \\).\n\nThus, the least value of \\( b \\) such that \\( b^2 + 2b - 15 \\le 0 \\) is \\(\\boxed{-5}\\).'
'To determine the time in Denver when the train arrives, we need to consider both the travel time and the time zone difference between New York and Denver.\n\n1. **Time Zone Difference**: New York is 2 hours ahead of Denver. Therefore, when it is 2 p.m. in New York, it is 12 p.m. (noon) in Denver.\n\n2. **Travel Time**: The train travels for 45 hours.\n\n3. **Calculate Arrival Time in New York Time**: \n   - The train leaves New York at 2 p.m.\n   - Adding 45 hours to 2 p.m. gives us the arrival time in New York time.\n   - 2 p.m. + 45 hours = 2 p.m. (next day) + 21 hours = 11 a.m. (two days later).\n\n4. **Convert to Denver Time**:\n   - Since New York is 2 hours ahead of Denver, we subtract 2 hours from the New York arrival time to get the Denver arrival time.\n   - 11 a.m. (New York time) - 2 hours = 9 a.m. (Denver time).\n\nTherefore, the train arrives in Denver at 9 a.m. Denver time.'

"To solve this problem, we need to determine Alice's speed and then calculate how long it would take her to run 50 meters.\n\n1. **Determine Alice's Time for 100 Meters:**\n   - Beatrice takes 25 seconds to complete the 100-meter race.\n   - Alice finishes 5 seconds before Beatrice, so Alice takes \\(25 - 5 = 20\\) seconds to complete the 100 meters.\n\n2. **Calculate Alice's Speed:**\n   - Alice's speed is the distance divided by the time. 'To find the value of \\( n \\) such that there exists a unique value of \\( m \\) for which the quadratic equation \\( x^2 + mx + (m+n) = 0 \\) has exactly one real solution, we need to follow these steps:\n\n1. **Understand the condition for one real solution**: A quadratic equation has exactly one real solution when its discriminant is zero. For the given quadratic equation \\( x^2 + mx + (m+n) = 0 \\), the discriminant \\(\\Delta\\) is given by:\n   \\[\n   \\Delta = m^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot (m+n) = m^2 - 4(m+n)\n   \\]\n\n2. **Set the discriminant to zero**: For the quadratic to have one real solution, we set the discriminant to zero:\n   \\[\n   m^2 - 4(m+n) = 0\n   \\]\n   Simplifying, we get:\n   \\[\n   m^2 - 4m - 4n = 0\n   \\]\n\n3. **Condition for a unique value of \\( m \\)**: The equation \\( m^2 - 4m - 4n = 0 \\) must have exactly one solution for \\( m \\). A quadratic equation has exactly one solution when its discriminant is zero. The discriminant of this equation is:\n   \\[\n   (-4)^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot (-4n) = 16 + 16n\n   \\]\n\n4. **Set this discriminant to zero**: For the equation \\( m^2 - 4m - 4n = 0 \\) to have exactly one solution, we set its discriminant to zero:\n   \\[\n   16 + 16n = 0\n   \\]\n\n5. **Solve for \\( n \\)**: Solving the equation \\( 16 + 16n = 0 \\) gives:\n   \\[\n   16n = -16 \\\\\n   n = -1\n   \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( n \\) is \\(\\boxed{-1}\\).'

"To solve the equation \\(\\log_{64^{\\frac{1}{3}}} 4^x = 1\\), we need to understand what this logarithmic expression means. The equation implies that the base \\(64^{\\frac{1}{3}}\\) raised to the power of 1 equals \\(4^x\\).\n\nLet's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Simplify the Base:**\n   - We start by simplifying the base \\(64^{\\frac{1}{3}}\\).\n   - Since \\(64 = 4^3\\), we have:\n     \\[\n     64^{\\frac{1}{3}} = (4^3)^{\\frac{1}{3}} = 4^{3 \\times \\frac{1}{3}} = 4^1 = 4.\n     \\]\n   - Therefore, the base of the logarithm simplifies to 4.\n\n2. **Rewrite the Logarithmic Equation:**\n   - The equation \\(\\log_{64^{\\frac{1}{3}}} 4^x = 1\\) now becomes:\n     \\[\n     \\log_4 4^x = 1.\n     \\]\n\n3. **Apply the Property of Logarithms:**\n   - We use the property of logarithms that states \\(\\log_b b^y = y\\).\n   - Applying this property, we have:\n     \\[\n     \\log_4 4^x = x.\n     \\]\n   - Since the equation is \\(\\log_4 4^x = 1\\), it follows that:\n     \\[\n     x = 1.\n     \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(x\\) is \\(\\boxed{1}\\)."

This means that if \\( f(a) = b \\), then \\( f^{-1}(b) = a \\).\n\nGiven:\n1. \\( f(2) = 6 \\), which implies \\( f^{-1}(6) = 2 \\).\n\nNow, we need to find \\( f^{-1}(f^{-1}(6)) \\):\n- We already know that \\( f^{-1}(6) = 2 \\).\n- Therefore, we need to find \\( f^{-1}(2) \\).\n\nTo find \\( f^{-1}(2) \\), we look for a value \\( x \\) such that \\( f(x) = 2 \\). "To solve this problem, we need to use Vieta's formulas, which relate the coefficients of a polynomial to sums and products of its roots.\n\nGiven the polynomial \\( p(x) = x^2 + ax + b \\), the roots are \\( 2a \\) and \\( b \\).\n\n1. **Sum of the roots**: According to Vieta's formulas, the sum of the roots is equal to the negation of the coefficient of \\( x \\), which gives us:\n   \\[\n   2a + b = -a\n   \\]\n   Rearranging this equation, we get:\n   \\[\n   3a + b = 0 \\quad \\text{(Equation 1)}\n   \\]\n\n2. **Product of the roots**: Vieta's formulas also tell us that the product of the roots is equal to the constant term \\( b \\), so:\n   \\[\n   (2a) \\cdot b = b\n   \\]\n   Since \\( b \\neq 0 \\) (otherwise, the roots wouldn't be distinct), we can divide both sides by \\( b \\) to get:\n   \\[\n   2a = 1 \\quad \\text{(Equation 2)}\n   \\]\n\nFrom Equation 2, we find:\n\\[\na = \\frac{1}{2}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\( a = \\frac{1}{2} \\) into Equation 1:\n\\[\n3\\left(\\frac{1}{2}\\right) + b = 0\n\\]\n\\[\n\\frac{3}{2} + b = 0\n\\]\n\\[\nb = -\\frac{3}{2}\n\\]\n\nFinally, we calculate \\( a + b \\):\n\\[\na + b = \\frac{1}{2} - \\frac{3}{2} = -1\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( a + b \\) is \\(\\boxed{-1}\\)."

Ten treeks weigh as much as three squigs and one goolee:\n   \\[\n   10T = 3S + G\n   \\]\n\n2. Two treeks and one goolee are equal in weight to one squig:\n   \\[\n   2T + G = S\n   \\]\n\nWe need to find the combined weight of how many treeks equals the weight of one squig, i.e., we need to express \\( S \\) in terms of \\( T \\).\n\nFrom the second equation, solve for \\( G \\):\n\\[\nG = S - 2T\n\\]\n\nSubstitute this expression for \\( G \\) into the first equation:\n\\[\n10T = 3S + (S - 2T)\n\\]\n\nSimplify the equation:\n\\[\n10T = 4S - 2T\n\\]\n\nAdd \\( 2T \\) to both sides to isolate terms involving \\( S \\):\n\\[\n12T = 4S\n\\]\n\nDivide both sides by 4 to solve for \\( S \\) in terms of \\( T \\):\n\\[\nS = 3T\n\\]\n\nThus, the combined weight of 3 treeks equals the weight of one squig. "Let \\( c \\) be the number of clowns and \\( h \\) be the number of horses. We know the following:\n\n1. Each clown has 1 head and 2 legs.\n2. Each horse has 1 head and 4 legs.\n3. The total number of heads is 10.\n4. The total number of legs is 30.\n\nFrom the information about heads, we can write the equation:\n\\[ c + h = 10 \\]\n\nFrom the information about legs, we can write the equation:\n\\[ 2c + 4h = 30 \\]\n\nWe now have a system of two equations:\n1. \\( c + h = 10 \\)\n2. \\( 2c + 4h = 30 \\)\n\nWe can solve this system by substitution or elimination. Let's use substitution:\n\nFrom the first equation, solve for \\( c \\):\n\\[ c = 10 - h \\]\n\nSubstitute \\( c = 10 - h \\) into the second equation:\n\\[ 2(10 - h) + 4h = 30 \\]\n\nSimplify and solve for \\( h \\):\n\\[ 20 - 2h + 4h = 30 \\]\n\\[ 20 + 2h = 30 \\]\n\\[ 2h = 10 \\]\n\\[ h = 5 \\]\n\nSo, there are 5 horses in the parade. To verify, substitute \\( h = 5 \\) back into the equation for \\( c \\):\n\\[ c = 10 - 5 = 5 \\]\n\nCheck the total number of legs:\n\\[ 2c + 4h = 2(5) + 4(5) = 10 + 20 = 30 \\]\n\nThe calculations are consistent with the given conditions. Therefore, the number of horses is \\(\\boxed{5}\\)."

The weight of \\( A \\) is \\( 40\\% \\) greater than the weight of \\( B \\). This means:\n   \\[\n   a = b + 0.4b = 1.4b\n   \\]\n\n2. 'To find the sum of all values of \\( a \\) for which the graphs of the equations \\( y = x^2 + a \\) and \\( y = ax \\) intersect at exactly one point, we need to analyze the intersection condition.\n\n1. **Set the equations equal to each other**:  \n   \\[\n   x^2 + a = ax\n   \\]\n\n2. **Rearrange to form a quadratic equation**:  \n   \\[\n   x^2 - ax + a = 0\n   \\]\n\n3. **Determine the condition for exactly one intersection point**:  \n   A quadratic equation has exactly one solution when its discriminant is zero. The discriminant \\(\\Delta\\) of the quadratic equation \\(x^2 - ax + a = 0\\) is given by:\n   \\[\n   \\Delta = b^2 - 4ac = (-a)^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot a = a^2 - 4a\n   \\]\n\n4. **Set the discriminant equal to zero**:  \n   \\[\n   a^2 - 4a = 0\n   \\]\n\n5. **Factor the equation**:  \n   \\[\n   a(a - 4) = 0\n   \\]\n\n6. **Solve for \\( a \\)**:  \n   The solutions are \\( a = 0 \\) and \\( a = 4 \\).\n\n7. **Calculate the sum of all values of \\( a \\)**:  \n   The sum of the values of \\( a \\) is:\n   \\[\n   0 + 4 = 4\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the sum of all values of \\( a \\) for which the graphs intersect at exactly one point is \\(\\boxed{4}\\).'
'To solve the inequality \\((2x+10)(x+3)<(3x+9)(x+8)\\), we first expand both sides.\n\n**Left side:**\n\\[\n(2x+10)(x+3) = 2x(x) + 2x(3) + 10(x) + 10(3) = 2x^2 + 6x + 10x + 30 = 2x^2 + 16x + 30\n\\]\n\n**Right side:**\n\\[\n(3x+9)(x+8) = 3x(x) + 3x(8) + 9(x) + 9(8) = 3x^2 + 24x + 9x + 72 = 3x^2 + 33x + 72\n\\]\n\nNow, we set up the inequality:\n\\[\n2x^2 + 16x + 30 < 3x^2 + 33x + 72\n\\]\n\nSubtract the left side from the right side:\n\\[\n0 < 3x^2 + 33x + 72 - 2x^2 - 16x - 30\n\\]\n\\[\n0 < x^2 + 17x + 42\n\\]\n\nWe need to solve the inequality:\n\\[\nx^2 + 17x + 42 > 0\n\\]\n\nFirst, find the roots of the quadratic equation \\(x^2 + 17x + 42 = 0\\) using the quadratic formula:\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\nwhere \\(a = 1\\), \\(b = 17\\), and \\(c = 42\\).\n\nCalculate the discriminant:\n\\[\nb^2 - 4ac = 17^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot 42 = 289 - 168 = 121\n\\]\n\nThe square root of 121 is 11, so the roots are:\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-17 \\pm 11}{2}\n\\]\n\nCalculate the roots:\n\\[\nx_1 = \\frac{-17 + 11}{2} = \\frac{-6}{2} = -3\n\\]\n\\[\nx_2 = \\frac{-17 - 11}{2} = \\frac{-28}{2} = -14\n\\]\n\nThe roots are \\(x = -3\\) and \\(x = -14\\). The quadratic \\(x^2 + 17x + 42\\) is positive outside the interval defined by these roots, since the parabola opens upwards (the coefficient of \\(x^2\\) is positive).\n\nThus, the solution to the inequality \\(x^2 + 17x + 42 > 0\\) is:\n\\[\nx \\in (-\\infty, -14) \\cup (-3, \\infty)\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the solution in interval notation is:\n\\[\n(-\\infty, -14) \\cup (-3, \\infty)\n\\]'
'To find the total value of the investment after five years, we need to calculate the compound interest over the 30 bi-monthly periods.\n\n1. **Initial Investment**: $P = \\$24,000$\n2. **Interest Rate per Period**: \\( r = 1\\% = 0.01 \\)\n3. **Number of Periods**: \\( n = 5 \\times 6 = 30 \\) (since there are 6 bi-monthly periods in a year)\n\nThe formula for compound interest is:\n\n\\[ A = P \\times (1 + r)^n \\]\n\nSubstituting the given values:\n\n\\[ A = 24000 \\times (1 + 0.01)^{30} \\]\n\n\\[ A = 24000 \\times (1.01)^{30} \\]\n\nNow, calculate \\( (1.01)^{30} \\):\n\nUsing a calculator, \\( (1.01)^{30} \\approx 1.34785 \\).\n\nNow, calculate the total amount:\n\n\\[ A = 24000 \\times 1.34785 \\]\n\n\\[ A \\approx 32,348.40 \\]\n\nRounding to the nearest whole number, the total value of the investment after five years is approximately \\(\\boxed{32,348}\\) dollars.'
'To determine the real values of \\( x \\) that are not in the domain of \\( f(x) = \\frac{1}{|x^2+3x-4|+|x^2+9x+20|} \\), we need to find when the denominator is equal to zero:\n\n1. **Identify the expressions inside the absolute values:**\n   - \\( x^2 + 3x - 4 \\)\n   - \\( x^2 + 9x + 20 \\)\n\n2. **Set the sum of the absolute values to zero:**\n   \\[\n   |x^2 + 3x - 4| + |x^2 + 9x + 20| = 0\n   \\]\n\n3. **Determine when each absolute value expression is zero:**\n   - \\( |x^2 + 3x - 4| = 0 \\) implies \\( x^2 + 3x - 4 = 0 \\)\n   - \\( |x^2 + 9x + 20| = 0 \\) implies \\( x^2 + 9x + 20 = 0 \\)\n\n4. **Solve the quadratic equations:**\n   - For \\( x^2 + 3x - 4 = 0 \\):\n     \\[\n     (x + 4)(x - 1) = 0 \\implies x = -4 \\text{ or } x = 1\n     \\]\n   - For \\( x^2 + 9x + 20 = 0 \\):\n     \\[\n     (x + 4)(x + 5) = 0 \\implies x = -4 \\text{ or } x = -5\n     \\]\n\n5. **Find the common solution where both expressions are zero:**\n   - The only common solution is \\( x = -4 \\).\n\nTherefore, the real value of \\( x \\) that makes the expression \\( |x^2+3x-4|+|x^2+9x+20| \\) equal to zero, thus making \\( f(x) \\) undefined, is:\n- \\( x = -4 \\)\n\nThus, the real value of \\( x \\) that is not in the domain of \\( f(x) \\) is \\( \\boxed{-4} \\).'
'To solve the problem, we need to evaluate the function \\( f(x) = x^{(x+1)}(x+2)^{(x+3)} \\) at the points \\( x = 0, -1, -2, \\) and \\( -3 \\), and then sum these values.\n\n1. **Evaluate \\( f(0) \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   f(0) = 0^{(0+1)}(0+2)^{(0+3)} = 0^1 \\cdot 2^3 = 0 \\cdot 8 = 0\n   \\]\n\n   Here, any non-zero number raised to the power of zero is 1, but since we have \\(0^1\\), the result is 0.\n\n2. **Evaluate \\( f(-1) \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   f(-1) = (-1)^{(-1+1)}(-1+2)^{(-1+3)} = (-1)^0 \\cdot 1^2 = 1 \\cdot 1 = 1\n   \\]\n\n   Since \\((-1)^0 = 1\\) and \\(1^2 = 1\\), the result is 1.\n\n3. **Evaluate \\( f(-2) \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   f(-2) = (-2)^{(-2+1)}(-2+2)^{(-2+3)} = (-2)^{-1} \\cdot 0^1\n   \\]\n\n   Since \\(0^1 = 0\\), the entire expression becomes:\n\n   \\[\n   f(-2) = \\frac{1}{-2} \\cdot 0 = 0\n   \\]\n\n   Any number multiplied by 0 is 0.\n\n4. **Evaluate \\( f(-3) \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   f(-3) = (-3)^{(-3+1)}(-3+2)^{(-3+3)} = (-3)^{-2} \\cdot (-1)^0\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   = \\frac{1}{(-3)^2} \\cdot 1 = \\frac{1}{9} \\cdot 1 = \\frac{1}{9}\n   \\]\n\n   Here, \\((-3)^{-2} = \\frac{1}{9}\\) and \\((-1)^0 = 1\\).\n\nNow, sum these values:\n\n\\[\nf(0) + f(-1) + f(-2) + f(-3) = 0 + 1 + 0 + \\frac{1}{9} = 1 + \\frac{1}{9} = \\frac{9}{9} + \\frac{1}{9} = \\frac{10}{9}\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( f(0) + f(-1) + f(-2) + f(-3) \\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{10}{9}}\\).'

Decreasing \\( a \\) by 5 gives \\( N \\), so \\( N = a - 5 \\).\n3. Increasing \\( b \\) by 5 gives \\( N \\), so \\( N = b + 5 \\).\n4. Multiplying \\( c \\) by 5 gives \\( N \\), so \\( N = 5c \\).\n\nWe have three equations for \\( N \\):\n\n\\[ N = a - 5 \\]\n\\[ N = b + 5 \\]\n\\[ N = 5c \\]\n\nSince all three expressions equal \\( N \\), we can set them equal to each other:\n\n1. \\( a - 5 = b + 5 \\)\n2. \\( b + 5 = 5c \\)\n\nFrom the first equation, solve for \\( a \\):\n\n\\[ a = b + 10 \\]\n\nFrom the second equation, solve for \\( b \\):\n\n\\[ b = 5c - 5 \\]\n\nNow substitute these expressions for \\( a \\) and \\( b \\) into the sum equation:\n\n\\[ a + b + c = 88 \\]\n\nSubstitute \\( a = b + 10 \\) and \\( b = 5c - 5 \\):\n\n\\[ (5c - 5) + 10 + (5c - 5) + c = 88 \\]\n\nSimplify:\n\n\\[ 5c - 5 + 10 + 5c - 5 + c = 88 \\]\n\\[ 11c = 88 \\]\n\nSolve for \\( c \\):\n\n\\[ c = 8 \\]\n\nNow substitute \\( c = 8 \\) back into the equation for \\( N \\):\n\n\\[ N = 5c = 5 \\times 8 = 40 \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( N \\) is \\(\\boxed{40}\\).'

'To compute \\(32^2 - 18^2\\), we can utilize the difference of squares formula, which states:\n\n\\[ a^2 - b^2 = (a - b)(a + b) \\]\n\nIn this case, we identify \\(a = 32\\) and \\(b = 18\\).\n\n1. **Calculate \\(a - b\\):**\n   \\[\n   32 - 18 = 14\n   \\]\n\n2. **Calculate \\(a + b\\):**\n   \\[\n   32 + 18 = 50\n   \\]\n\n3. **Apply the Difference of Squares Formula:**\n   \\[\n   32^2 - 18^2 = (32 - 18)(32 + 18) = 14 \\times 50\n   \\]\n\n4. **Compute the Product:**\n   \\[\n   14 \\times 50 = 700\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the result of \\(32^2 - 18^2\\) is \\(\\boxed{700}\\).'
'To find the fiftieth term of the arithmetic sequence, we need to determine the common difference \\( d \\) and the first term \\( a_1 \\).\n\nGiven:\n- The second term \\( a_2 = 2 \\).\n- The ninth term \\( a_9 = 30 \\).\n\nUsing the formula for the nth term of an arithmetic sequence:\n\\[ a_n = a_1 + (n-1) \\cdot d \\]\n\nFor the second term:\n\\[ a_2 = a_1 + 1 \\cdot d = 2 \\]\n\\[ a_1 + d = 2 \\quad \\text{(Equation 1)} \\]\n\nFor the ninth term:\n\\[ a_9 = a_1 + 8 \\cdot d = 30 \\]\n\\[ a_1 + 8d = 30 \\quad \\text{(Equation 2)} \\]\n\nSubtract Equation 1 from Equation 2 to find \\( d \\):\n\\[ (a_1 + 8d) - (a_1 + d) = 30 - 2 \\]\n\\[ 7d = 28 \\]\n\\[ d = 4 \\]\n\nNow, substitute \\( d = 4 \\) back into Equation 1 to find \\( a_1 \\):\n\\[ a_1 + 4 = 2 \\]\n\\[ a_1 = 2 - 4 \\]\n\\[ a_1 = -2 \\]\n\nNow, we can find the fiftieth term \\( a_{50} \\):\n\\[ a_{50} = a_1 + 49 \\cdot d \\]\n\\[ a_{50} = -2 + 49 \\cdot 4 \\]\n\\[ a_{50} = -2 + 196 \\]\n\\[ a_{50} = 194 \\]\n\nTherefore, the fiftieth term of the sequence is \\(\\boxed{194}\\).'

This is a downward-opening parabola with its vertex at \\((-1, 1)\\).\n\n2. **Shift 1 Unit to the Right**: Shifting the parabola 1 unit to the right changes the equation to \\( y = -(x)^2 + 1 \\). The vertex is now at \\((0, 1)\\).\n\n3. **Shift 5 Units Down**: Shifting the parabola 5 units down changes the equation to \\( y = -(x)^2 - 4 \\). The vertex is now at \\((0, -4)\\).\n\n4. **Rotate 180 Degrees About the Vertex**: Rotating the parabola 180 degrees about its vertex changes the direction of the parabola from opening downwards to opening upwards.
