'To factor the expression \\(24x^2 - 19x - 35\\) as \\((Ax - 5)(2Bx + C)\\), we need to expand the right-hand side and match coefficients with the original quadratic expression.\n\nExpanding \\((Ax - 5)(2Bx + C)\\), we get:\n\\[\n(Ax - 5)(2Bx + C) = A(2Bx + C)x - 5(2Bx + C)\n\\]\n\\[\n= 2ABx^2 + ACx - 10Bx - 5C\n\\]\n\\[\n= 2ABx^2 + (AC - 10B)x - 5C\n\\]\n\nNow, we match the coefficients with the original expression \\(24x^2 - 19x - 35\\):\n1. "To factor the polynomial \\(-16x^4 + x^2 + 2x + 1\\) into two quadratic polynomials with integer coefficients, we need to find polynomials of the form \\((ax^2 + bx + c)(dx^2 + ex + f)\\) such that their product equals the given polynomial. 'To solve the inequality \\( x^{-1} > x \\) for positive integer values of \\( x \\), we start by rewriting the inequality:\n\n1. The inequality is given as \\( x^{-1} > x \\), which can be rewritten as \\( \\frac{1}{x} > x \\).\n\n2. Multiply both sides by \\( x \\) (assuming \\( x > 0 \\) to avoid division by zero), resulting in:\n   \\[\n   1 > x^2\n   \\]\n\n3. The inequality \\( 1 > x^2 \\) implies that \\( x^2 < 1 \\).\n\n4. Since \\( x \\) is a positive integer, we need to find positive integer values of \\( x \\) such that \\( x^2 < 1 \\).\n\n5. The only positive integer \\( x \\) that satisfies \\( x^2 < 1 \\) is \\( x = 1 \\), because:\n   - If \\( x = 1 \\), then \\( x^2 = 1 \\), which does not satisfy \\( x^2 < 1 \\).\n   - However, since we are looking for \\( x^2 < 1 \\), and \\( x = 1 \\) is the only positive integer that comes close, we need to reconsider the interpretation. The inequality \\( x^2 < 1 \\) implies \\( x \\) must be less than 1, but since \\( x \\) is a positive integer, there are no positive integers less than 1.\n\nTherefore, there are no positive integer values of \\( x \\) for which \\( x^{-1} > x \\) holds. The answer is \\( \\boxed{0} \\).'
'To solve for \\( a + b \\), we need to use the given conditions for the piecewise function \\( f(x) \\).\n\n1. **Condition for \\( x \\le -4 \\):**\n\n   Given \\( f(-4) = -\\frac{60}{13} \\), we use the first piece of the function:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{a}{b}(-4) = -\\frac{60}{13}.\n   \\]\n   Simplifying, we get:\n   \\[\n   -\\frac{4a}{b} = -\\frac{60}{13}.\n   \\]\n   Multiplying both sides by \\(-1\\) and then by \\( b \\), we have:\n   \\[\n   4a = \\frac{60}{13}b.\n   \\]\n   Solving for \\( a \\), we get:\n   \\[\n   a = \\frac{15}{13}b.\n   \\]\n\n2. **Condition for \\( x > -4 \\):**\n\n   Given \\( f(4) = 3120 \\), we use the second piece of the function:\n   \\[\n   ab(4)^2 = 3120.\n   \\]\n   Simplifying, we have:\n   \\[\n   16ab = 3120.\n   \\]\n   Solving for \\( ab \\), we get:\n   \\[\n   ab = 195.\n   \\]\n\n3. **Substitute \\( a = \\frac{15}{13}b \\) into \\( ab = 195 \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   \\left(\\frac{15}{13}b\\right)b = 195.\n   \\]\n   Simplifying, we have:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{15}{13}b^2 = 195.\n   \\]\n   Multiplying both sides by 13, we get:\n   \\[\n   15b^2 = 2535.\n   \\]\n   Dividing both sides by 15, we find:\n   \\[\n   b^2 = 169.\n   \\]\n   Taking the square root of both sides, we get:\n   \\[\n   b = 13.\n   \\]\n\n4. **Find \\( a \\) using \\( a = \\frac{15}{13}b \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   a = \\frac{15}{13} \\times 13 = 15.\n   \\]\n\n5. **Calculate \\( a + b \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   a + b = 15 + 13 = 28.\n   \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( a + b \\) is \\(\\boxed{28}\\).'
'To find the time \\( t \\) when the ball hits the ground, we need to solve the equation \\( y = -16t^2 - 60t + 54 = 0 \\).\n\nThis is a quadratic equation in the standard form \\( at^2 + bt + c = 0 \\), where \\( a = -16 \\), \\( b = -60 \\), and \\( c = 54 \\).\n\nWe can use the quadratic formula to solve for \\( t \\):\n\n\\[\nt = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the values of \\( a \\), \\( b \\), and \\( c \\) into the formula, we get:\n\n\\[\nt = \\frac{-(-60) \\pm \\sqrt{(-60)^2 - 4(-16)(54)}}{2(-16)}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nt = \\frac{60 \\pm \\sqrt{3600 + 3456}}{-32}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nt = \\frac{60 \\pm \\sqrt{7056}}{-32}\n\\]\n\nCalculate the square root of 7056:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{7056} = 84\n\\]\n\nNow substitute back into the equation:\n\n\\[\nt = \\frac{60 \\pm 84}{-32}\n\\]\n\nThis gives us two possible solutions for \\( t \\):\n\n1. \\( t = \\frac{60 + 84}{-32} = \\frac{144}{-32} = -4.5 \\)\n2. \\( t = \\frac{60 - 84}{-32} = \\frac{-24}{-32} = 0.75 \\)\n\nSince time cannot be negative, we discard \\( t = -4.5 \\).\n\nThus, the ball will hit the ground in \\( t = 0.75 \\) seconds.\n\nThe answer is \\( \\boxed{0.75} \\).'
'To evaluate the expression \\(\\lfloor 14.6 \\rfloor - \\lceil -14.6 \\rceil\\), we need to understand the floor and ceiling functions:\n\n1. The floor function \\(\\lfloor x \\rfloor\\) gives the greatest integer less than or equal to \\(x\\). For \\(14.6\\), the greatest integer less than or equal to \\(14.6\\) is \\(14\\). Therefore, \\(\\lfloor 14.6 \\rfloor = 14\\).\n\n2. The ceiling function \\(\\lceil x \\rceil\\) gives the smallest integer greater than or equal to \\(x\\). For \\(-14.6\\), the smallest integer greater than or equal to \\(-14.6\\) is \\(-14\\). Therefore, \\(\\lceil -14.6 \\rceil = -14\\).\n\nNow, we substitute these values into the expression:\n\n\\[\n\\lfloor 14.6 \\rfloor - \\lceil -14.6 \\rceil = 14 - (-14)\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the expression:\n\n\\[\n14 - (-14) = 14 + 14 = 28\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of the expression is \\(\\boxed{28}\\).'
'To find the percent increase in the area of the TV screen when each dimension is increased by 20%, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Calculate the original area:**\n   The original dimensions of the TV screen are 24 inches by 16 inches. Therefore, the original area is:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Original Area} = 24 \\times 16 = 384 \\text{ square inches}\n   \\]\n\n2. **Calculate the new dimensions:**\n   Each dimension is increased by 20%. Therefore, the new dimensions are:\n   \\[\n   \\text{New Length} = 24 + 0.2 \\times 24 = 24 \\times 1.2 = 28.8 \\text{ inches}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   \\text{New Width} = 16 + 0.2 \\times 16 = 16 \\times 1.2 = 19.2 \\text{ inches}\n   \\]\n\n3. **Calculate the new area:**\n   Using the new dimensions, the new area is:\n   \\[\n   \\text{New Area} = 28.8 \\times 19.2 = 552.96 \\text{ square inches}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Calculate the increase in area:**\n   The increase in area is the difference between the new area and the original area:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Increase in Area} = 552.96 - 384 = 168.96 \\text{ square inches}\n   \\]\n\n5. **Calculate the percent increase in area:**\n   The percent increase in area is given by the formula:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Percent Increase} = \\left(\\frac{\\text{Increase in Area}}{\\text{Original Area}}\\right) \\times 100\\%\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   \\text{Percent Increase} = \\left(\\frac{168.96}{384}\\right) \\times 100\\% \\approx 44\\%\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the area of the TV screen is increased by approximately 44%.'
"To expand the expression \\((q-5)(3r+6)\\), we will apply the distributive property, which involves multiplying each term in the first parenthesis by each term in the second parenthesis. Here's the step-by-step process:\n\n1. **Distribute \\(q\\) to both terms in the second parenthesis:**\n\n   - Multiply \\(q\\) by \\(3r\\): \n     \\[\n     q \\cdot 3r = 3qr\n     \\]\n\n   - Multiply \\(q\\) by \\(6\\): \n     \\[\n     q \\cdot 6 = 6q\n     \\]\n\n   So, the result of distributing \\(q\\) is:\n   \\[\n   3qr + 6q\n   \\]\n\n2. **Distribute \\(-5\\) to both terms in the second parenthesis:**\n\n   - Multiply \\(-5\\) by \\(3r\\): \n     \\[\n     -5 \\cdot 3r = -15r\n     \\]\n\n   - Multiply \\(-5\\) by \\(6\\): \n     \\[\n     -5 \\cdot 6 = -30\n     \\]\n\n   So, the result of distributing \\(-5\\) is:\n   \\[\n   -15r - 30\n   \\]\n\n3. **Combine all the terms from the distributions:**\n\n   Combine the results from steps 1 and 2:\n   \\[\n   3qr + 6q - 15r - 30\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the expanded form of \\((q-5)(3r+6)\\) is:\n\\[\n3qr + 6q - 15r - 30\n\\]"
'To determine the total distance the ball has traveled when it hits the floor for the sixth time, we need to consider both the downward and upward movements of the ball.\n\n1. **Initial Drop:**\n   - The ball is initially dropped from a height of 16 feet. This is the first fall.\n\n2. **Subsequent Bounces:**\n   - After the first fall, the ball bounces back to half the height it fell from. So, after falling 16 feet, it bounces back to \\( \\frac{16}{2} = 8 \\) feet.\n   - It then falls again from 8 feet, bounces back to \\( \\frac{8}{2} = 4 \\) feet.\n   - It falls from 4 feet, bounces back to \\( \\frac{4}{2} = 2 \\) feet.\n   - It falls from 2 feet, bounces back to \\( \\frac{2}{2} = 1 \\) foot.\n   - It falls from 1 foot, bounces back to \\( \\frac{1}{2} = 0.5 \\) feet.\n   - It falls from 0.5 feet, bounces back to \\( \\frac{0.5}{2} = 0.25 \\) feet.\n\n3. **Total Distance Calculation:**\n   - The ball hits the floor for the sixth time after the last fall from 0.5 feet. We need to sum up all the distances traveled:\n   - First fall: 16 feet\n   - First bounce up and second fall: \\( 8 + 8 = 16 \\) feet\n   - Second bounce up and third fall: \\( 4 + 4 = 8 \\) feet\n   - Third bounce up and fourth fall: \\( 2 + 2 = 4 \\) feet\n   - Fourth bounce up and fifth fall: \\( 1 + 1 = 2 \\) feet\n   - Fifth bounce up and sixth fall: \\( 0.5 + 0.5 = 1 \\) foot\n\n4. **Total Distance:**\n   - Total distance traveled = \\( 16 + 16 + 8 + 4 + 2 + 1 = 47 \\) feet.\n\nTherefore, the ball will have traveled a total of 47 feet when it hits the floor for the sixth time.'

'To evaluate the expression \\(\\log_{5^2}5^4\\), we can use the properties of logarithms and the given hint.\n\n1. The expression is \\(\\log_{5^2}5^4\\), which involves a logarithm with base \\(5^2\\) and argument \\(5^4\\).\n\n2. We can apply the logarithmic identity \\(\\log_{a^b}c^d = \\frac{d}{b} \\log_a c\\). In this case, \\(a = 5\\), \\(b = 2\\), \\(c = 5\\), and \\(d = 4\\).\n\n3. 'To find the number of \\( y \\)-intercepts of the parabola given by the equation \\( x = y^2 - 4y - 1 \\), we need to determine where the graph intersects the \\( y \\)-axis. This occurs when \\( x = 0 \\).\n\nSetting \\( x = 0 \\) in the equation, we have:\n\n\\[ 0 = y^2 - 4y - 1. \\]\n\nThis is a quadratic equation in \\( y \\). To find the \\( y \\)-values where the graph intersects the \\( y \\)-axis, we need to solve this quadratic equation. The number of solutions to this equation will tell us the number of \\( y \\)-intercepts.\n\nThe quadratic equation is:\n\n\\[ y^2 - 4y - 1 = 0. \\]\n\nWe can solve this using the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[ y = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}, \\]\n\nwhere \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = -4 \\), and \\( c = -1 \\).\n\nFirst, calculate the discriminant:\n\n\\[ b^2 - 4ac = (-4)^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot (-1) = 16 + 4 = 20. \\]\n\nSince the discriminant is positive (\\( 20 > 0 \\)), the quadratic equation has two distinct real solutions. Therefore, the graph of the parabola has two \\( y \\)-intercepts.\n\nThus, the number of \\( y \\)-intercepts is \\(\\boxed{2}\\).'
"To solve the problem, we need to factor the quadratic expression \\(6y^2 - y - 51\\) into the form \\((3Ay + B)(y - C)\\), where \\(A\\), \\(B\\), and \\(C\\) are positive integers. Then, we will find the value of \\((AC)^2 - B\\).\n\nFirst, let's expand the expression \\((3Ay + B)(y - C)\\):\n\n\\[\n(3Ay + B)(y - C) = 3Ay^2 - 3ACy + By - BC\n\\]\n\nThis must be equal to the original expression \\(6y^2 - y - 51\\). By comparing coefficients, we have:\n\n1. \\(3A = 6\\)\n2. \\(-3AC + B = -1\\)\n3. \\(-BC = -51\\)\n\nFrom the first equation, \\(3A = 6\\), we find \\(A = 2\\).\n\nSubstituting \\(A = 2\\) into the third equation \\(-BC = -51\\), we get:\n\n\\[\nBC = 51\n\\]\n\nThe factor pairs of 51 are \\((1, 51)\\), \\((3, 17)\\), \\((17, 3)\\), and \\((51, 1)\\). Since \\(B\\) and \\(C\\) are positive integers, we need to check which pair satisfies the second equation \\(-3AC + B = -1\\).\n\nSubstituting \\(A = 2\\) into the second equation, we have:\n\n\\[\n-3(2)C + B = -1 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad -6C + B = -1 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad B = 6C - 1\n\\]\n\nNow, let's test the factor pairs:\n\n1. If \\(C = 3\\), then \\(B = 6(3) - 1 = 18 - 1 = 17\\). This satisfies \\(BC = 51\\) because \\(17 \\times 3 = 51\\).\n\nThus, the values are \\(A = 2\\), \\(B = 17\\), and \\(C = 3\\).\n\nNow, calculate \\((AC)^2 - B\\):\n\n\\[\nAC = 2 \\times 3 = 6\n\\]\n\n\\[\n(AC)^2 = 6^2 = 36\n\\]\n\n\\[\n(AC)^2 - B = 36 - 17 = 19\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\((AC)^2 - B\\) is \\(\\boxed{19}\\)."

The expression inside the absolute value is \\(x - 5\\).\n2. Since we are given that \\(x < 5\\), it follows that \\(x - 5\\) is negative.\n3. When the expression inside the absolute value is negative, the absolute value function changes the sign of the expression. Therefore, \\(|x - 5| = -(x - 5)\\).\n4. Substitute this into the original expression: \n   \\[\n   5x - |x - 5| = 5x - (-(x - 5))\n   \\]\n5. Simplify the expression by distributing the negative sign:\n   \\[\n   5x - (-(x - 5)) = 5x + (x - 5)\n   \\]\n6. "To solve this problem, we need to establish the relationships between the costs of cookies, brownies, and cupcakes based on the given information.\n\n1. **Six cookies cost the same as 2 brownies.**\n   - Let's denote the cost of one cookie as \\( C \\) and the cost of one brownie as \\( B \\).\n   - From the information, we have: \n     \\[\n     6C = 2B\n     \\]\n   - Simplifying this equation, we find:\n     \\[\n     3C = B\n     \\]\n   - This means the cost of one brownie is equivalent to the cost of three cookies.\n\n2. **Four brownies cost the same as 10 cupcakes.**\n   - Let's denote the cost of one cupcake as \\( K \\).\n   - From the information, we have:\n     \\[\n     4B = 10K\n     \\]\n   - Simplifying this equation, we find:\n     \\[\n     2B = 5K\n     \\]\n   - This means the cost of two brownies is equivalent to the cost of five cupcakes.\n\n3. **Determine the cost of 18 cookies in terms of cupcakes.**\n   - We know from the first relationship that \\( B = 3C \\). Therefore, the cost of 18 cookies is:\n     \\[\n     18C = 6B\n     \\]\n   - From the second relationship, we know \\( 2B = 5K \\), so:\n     \\[\n     6B = 3 \\times 2B = 3 \\times 5K = 15K\n     \\]\n   - Therefore, the cost of 18 cookies is equivalent to the cost of 15 cupcakes.\n\nThus, Bob can buy \\(\\boxed{15}\\) cupcakes for the price of eighteen cookies."
'To find the maximum value of the quadratic function \\( f(x) = -x^2 - 8x + 12 \\), we need to determine the vertex of the parabola. Since the coefficient of \\( x^2 \\) is negative, the parabola opens downwards, and the maximum value occurs at the vertex.\n\nThe formula for the \\( x \\)-coordinate of the vertex of a quadratic function \\( ax^2 + bx + c \\) is given by:\n\n\\[\nx = -\\frac{b}{2a}\n\\]\n\nFor the function \\( f(x) = -x^2 - 8x + 12 \\), we have \\( a = -1 \\) and \\( b = -8 \\). Substituting these values into the formula gives:\n\n\\[\nx = -\\frac{-8}{2 \\times -1} = -\\frac{8}{-2} = 4\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\( x = 4 \\) back into the function to find the maximum value:\n\n\\[\nf(4) = -(4)^2 - 8(4) + 12\n\\]\n\nCalculate each term:\n\n\\[\n-(4)^2 = -16\n\\]\n\\[\n-8(4) = -32\n\\]\n\nSo,\n\n\\[\nf(4) = -16 - 32 + 12 = -36\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the maximum value of the function \\( f(x) = -x^2 - 8x + 12 \\) is \\(-36\\).'
"To find the value of \\(\\frac{d}{c}\\) given the equations \\(d - 6c = 4\\) and \\(2d - 9c = 20\\), we can solve the system of equations using the method of elimination.\n\nFirst, let's write down the given equations:\n\n1. \\(d - 6c = 4\\)\n2. \\(2d - 9c = 20\\)\n\nTo eliminate \\(d\\), we can multiply the first equation by 2 to align the coefficients of \\(d\\):\n\n\\[\n2(d - 6c) = 2 \\times 4\n\\]\n\nThis gives us:\n\n\\[\n2d - 12c = 8\n\\]\n\nNow, we have the system:\n\n1. \\(2d - 12c = 8\\)\n2. \\(2d - 9c = 20\\)\n\nNext, subtract the first equation from the second equation to eliminate \\(d\\):\n\n\\[\n(2d - 9c) - (2d - 12c) = 20 - 8\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n-9c + 12c = 12\n\\]\n\n\\[\n3c = 12\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\(c\\), we get:\n\n\\[\nc = 4\n\\]\n\nNow that we have \\(c = 4\\), substitute it back into the first equation to find \\(d\\):\n\n\\[\nd - 6(4) = 4\n\\]\n\n\\[\nd - 24 = 4\n\\]\n\n\\[\nd = 28\n\\]\n\nNow, we have \\(d = 28\\) and \\(c = 4\\). We can find \\(\\frac{d}{c}\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{d}{c} = \\frac{28}{4} = 7\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(\\frac{d}{c}\\) is \\(\\boxed{7}\\)."
"To solve the problem, we need to find the value of \\( c + \\frac{1}{a} \\) given the conditions:\n\n1. \\( a + \\frac{1}{b} = \\frac{22}{7} \\)\n2. \\( b + \\frac{1}{c} = 8 \\)\n3. \\( abc = 21 \\)\n\nLet's solve these equations step by step.\n\n### Step 1: Solve for \\( a \\) and \\( b \\)\n\nFrom the first equation:\n\\[\na + \\frac{1}{b} = \\frac{22}{7}\n\\]\nMultiply through by \\( b \\) to clear the fraction:\n\\[\nab + 1 = \\frac{22}{7}b\n\\]\nRearrange to find:\n\\[\nab - \\frac{22}{7}b = -1\n\\]\n\\[\nb(a - \\frac{22}{7}) = -1\n\\]\nThus:\n\\[\nb = -\\frac{1}{a - \\frac{22}{7}}\n\\]\n\n### Step 2: Solve for \\( b \\) and \\( c \\)\n\nFrom the second equation:\n\\[\nb + \\frac{1}{c} = 8\n\\]\nMultiply through by \\( c \\) to clear the fraction:\n\\[\nbc + 1 = 8c\n\\]\nRearrange to find:\n\\[\nbc - 8c = -1\n\\]\n\\[\nc(b - 8) = -1\n\\]\nThus:\n\\[\nc = -\\frac{1}{b - 8}\n\\]\n\n### Step 3: Use the product condition\n\nWe know:\n\\[\nabc = 21\n\\]\n\n### Step 4: Solve the system\n\nSubstitute the expressions for \\( b \\) and \\( c \\) into the product condition:\n\\[\na \\left(-\\frac{1}{a - \\frac{22}{7}}\\right) \\left(-\\frac{1}{b - 8}\\right) = 21\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\\[\n\\frac{a}{(a - \\frac{22}{7})(b - 8)} = 21\n\\]\n\n### Step 5: Solve for specific values\n\nSince \\( a, b, c \\) are integers, let's test possible integer values for \\( a \\).\n\n#### Assume \\( a = 3 \\)\n\nSubstitute \\( a = 3 \\) into the first equation:\n\\[\n3 + \\frac{1}{b} = \\frac{22}{7}\n\\]\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{b} = \\frac{22}{7} - 3 = \\frac{22}{7} - \\frac{21}{7} = \\frac{1}{7}\n\\]\nThus, \\( b = 7 \\).\n\n#### Check \\( b = 7 \\) in the second equation\n\nSubstitute \\( b = 7 \\) into the second equation:\n\\[\n7 + \\frac{1}{c} = 8\n\\]\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{c} = 1 \\Rightarrow c = 1\n\\]\n\n#### Verify the product condition\n\nCheck if \\( abc = 21 \\):\n\\[\n3 \\times 7 \\times 1 = 21\n\\]\nThis is correct.\n\n### Step 6: Find \\( c + \\frac{1}{a} \\)\n\nNow, calculate:\n\\[\nc + \\frac{1}{a} = 1 + \\frac{1}{3} = \\frac{3}{3} + \\frac{1}{3} = \\frac{4}{3}\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( c + \\frac{1}{a} \\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{4}{3}}\\)."
'To solve this problem, we need to find the greatest three-digit number "abc" such that the digits \\(4, a, b\\) form a geometric sequence and the digits \\(b, c, 5\\) form an arithmetic sequence.\n\n### Step 1: Analyze the Geometric Sequence \\(4, a, b\\)\n\nIn a geometric sequence, the ratio between consecutive terms is constant. Let the common ratio be \\(r\\). Therefore, we have:\n\\[ a = 4r \\]\n\\[ b = 4r^2 \\]\n\nSince \\(a\\) and \\(b\\) are digits, they must be integers between 0 and 9. This means \\(4r\\) and \\(4r^2\\) must also be integers and digits.\n\n### Step 2: Analyze the Arithmetic Sequence \\(b, c, 5\\)\n\nIn an arithmetic sequence, the difference between consecutive terms is constant. Let the common difference be \\(d\\). Therefore, we have:\n\\[ c = b + d \\]\n\\[ 5 = c + d \\]\n\nFrom the second equation, we get:\n\\[ d = 5 - c \\]\n\nSubstituting into the first equation:\n\\[ c = b + (5 - c) \\]\n\\[ 2c = b + 5 \\]\n\\[ c = \\frac{b + 5}{2} \\]\n\nSince \\(c\\) is a digit, \\(\\frac{b + 5}{2}\\) must be an integer, meaning \\(b + 5\\) must be even.\n\n### Step 3: Find Possible Values for \\(a\\), \\(b\\), and \\(c\\)\n\n1. **Geometric Sequence Constraints:**\n   - \\(a = 4r\\) and \\(b = 4r^2\\) must be digits.\n   - Possible values for \\(r\\) are 0.5, 1, 1.5, and 2 (since \\(4r\\) and \\(4r^2\\) must be digits).\n\n2. **Arithmetic Sequence Constraints:**\n   - \\(c = \\frac{b + 5}{2}\\) must be a digit.\n\nLet\'s evaluate each possible \\(r\\):\n\n- **\\(r = 1\\):**\n  - \\(a = 4 \\times 1 = 4\\)\n  - \\(b = 4 \\times 1^2 = 4\\)\n  - \\(c = \\frac{4 + 5}{2} = 4.5\\) (not an integer)\n\n- **\\(r = 1.5\\):**\n  - \\(a = 4 \\times 1.5 = 6\\)\n  - \\(b = 4 \\times 1.5^2 = 9\\)\n  - \\(c = \\frac{9 + 5}{2} = 7\\) (valid)\n\n- **\\(r = 2\\):**\n  - \\(a = 4 \\times 2 = 8\\)\n  - \\(b = 4 \\times 2^2 = 16\\) (not a digit)\n\n- **\\(r = 0.5\\):**\n  - \\(a = 4 \\times 0.5 = 2\\)\n  - \\(b = 4 \\times 0.5^2 = 1\\)\n  - \\(c = \\frac{1 + 5}{2} = 3\\) (valid)\n\n### Step 4: Determine the Greatest Number\n\nFrom the valid sequences:\n- For \\(r = 1.5\\), the number is 496.\n- For \\(r = 0.5\\), the number is 213.\n\nThe greatest number is 496.\n\nThus, the greatest three-digit number "abc" is \\(\\boxed{496}\\).'
'To express the quadratic \\( x^2 - 6x + 66 \\) in the form \\( (x+b)^2 + c \\), we need to complete the square.\n\n1. Start with the quadratic expression: \\( x^2 - 6x + 66 \\).\n\n2. To complete the square, focus on the \\( x^2 - 6x \\) part. The coefficient of \\( x \\) is \\(-6\\). \n\n3. Take half of \\(-6\\), which is \\(-3\\), and square it: \n   \\[\n   \\left(\\frac{-6}{2}\\right)^2 = (-3)^2 = 9\n   \\]\n\n4. Add and subtract this square inside the expression to complete the square:\n   \\[\n   x^2 - 6x + 9 - 9 + 66\n   \\]\n\n5. Rewrite the expression as a perfect square and simplify:\n   \\[\n   (x-3)^2 + (66 - 9) = (x-3)^2 + 57\n   \\]\n\n6. Now, the quadratic is in the form \\( (x+b)^2 + c \\), where \\( b = -3 \\) and \\( c = 57 \\).\n\n7. Calculate \\( b + c \\):\n   \\[\n   b + c = -3 + 57 = 54\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( b+c \\) is \\(\\boxed{54}\\).'
"To determine which letters could be portions of the graph of a function, we apply the vertical line test. A letter can be part of the graph of a function if no vertical line intersects the letter at more than one point.\n\nLet's analyze each letter:\n\n1. **A** - Passes the vertical line test.\n2. **B** - Fails the vertical line test (vertical line intersects at two points).\n3. **C** - Passes the vertical line test.\n4. **D** - Fails the vertical line test (vertical line intersects at two points).\n5. **E** - Passes the vertical line test.\n6. **F** - Passes the vertical line test.\n7. **G** - Passes the vertical line test.\n8. **H** - Passes the vertical line test.\n9. **I** - Passes the vertical line test.\n10. **J** - Passes the vertical line test.\n11. **K** - Passes the vertical line test.\n12. **L** - Passes the vertical line test.\n13. **M** - Passes the vertical line test.\n14. **N** - Passes the vertical line test.\n15. **O** - Fails the vertical line test (vertical line intersects at multiple points).\n16. **P** - Fails the vertical line test (vertical line intersects at two points).\n17. **Q** - Fails the vertical line test (vertical line intersects at multiple points).\n18. **R** - Passes the vertical line test.\n19. **S** - Passes the vertical line test.\n20. **T** - Passes the vertical line test.\n21. **U** - Passes the vertical line test.\n22. **V** - Passes the vertical line test.\n23. **W** - Passes the vertical line test.\n24. **X** - Fails the vertical line test (vertical line intersects at two points).\n25. **Y** - Passes the vertical line test.\n26. **Z** - Passes the vertical line test.\n\nBased on this analysis, the letters that could be portions of the graph of a function are:\n\n**ACEFGHIJKLMNRSTUVWYZ**\n\nTherefore, the answer is: **ACEFGHIJKLMNRSTUVWYZ**."
'To solve the inequality \\( x^2 - 5x - 4 \\le 10 \\), we first rewrite it in a form that sets the inequality to zero:\n\n1. **Rewrite the Inequality:**\n   \\[\n   x^2 - 5x - 4 \\le 10\n   \\]\n   Subtract 10 from both sides:\n   \\[\n   x^2 - 5x - 14 \\le 0\n   \\]\n\n2. **Solve the Corresponding Equation:**\n   We solve the equation \\( x^2 - 5x - 14 = 0 \\) using the quadratic formula:\n   \\[\n   x = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n   \\]\n   where \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = -5 \\), and \\( c = -14 \\).\n\n3. **Calculate the Discriminant:**\n   \\[\n   b^2 - 4ac = (-5)^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot (-14) = 25 + 56 = 81\n   \\]\n\n4. **Find the Roots:**\n   \\[\n   x = \\frac{5 \\pm \\sqrt{81}}{2}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   x = \\frac{5 \\pm 9}{2}\n   \\]\n   This gives the solutions:\n   \\[\n   x = \\frac{5 + 9}{2} = 7 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad x = \\frac{5 - 9}{2} = -2\n   \\]\n\n5. **Test Intervals Around the Roots:**\n   We need to determine where the inequality \\( x^2 - 5x - 14 \\le 0 \\) holds by testing intervals around the roots \\( x = -2 \\) and \\( x = 7 \\).\n\n   - **Interval \\((- \\infty, -2)\\):** Choose \\( x = -3 \\).\n     \\[\n     (-3)^2 - 5(-3) - 14 = 9 + 15 - 14 = 10 > 0\n     \\]\n     The inequality does not hold.\n\n   - **Interval \\((-2, 7)\\):** Choose \\( x = 0 \\).\n     \\[\n     0^2 - 5(0) - 14 = -14 \\le 0\n     \\]\n     The inequality holds.\n\n   - **Interval \\((7, \\infty)\\):** Choose \\( x = 8 \\).\n     \\[\n     8^2 - 5(8) - 14 = 64 - 40 - 14 = 10 > 0\n     \\]\n     The inequality does not hold.\n\n6. **Conclusion:**\n   The inequality \\( x^2 - 5x - 14 \\le 0 \\) holds in the interval \\([-2, 7]\\).\n\nTherefore, the solution in interval notation is:\n\\[\n[-2, 7]\n\\]'
"To solve for \\( A + M + C \\), we start by analyzing the given information and the equation derived from the sum of the two numbers \\( AMC10 \\) and \\( AMC12 \\).\n\n1. The numbers can be expressed as:\n   - \\( AMC10 = 10000A + 1000M + 100C + 10 \\)\n   - \\( AMC12 = 10000A + 1000M + 100C + 12 \\)\n\n2. The sum of these numbers is given as:\n   \\[\n   (10000A + 1000M + 100C + 10) + (10000A + 1000M + 100C + 12) = 123422\n   \\]\n\n3. Simplifying the equation:\n   \\[\n   20000A + 2000M + 200C + 22 = 123422\n   \\]\n\n4. Subtract 22 from both sides to isolate the terms involving \\( A \\), \\( M \\), and \\( C \\):\n   \\[\n   20000A + 2000M + 200C = 123400\n   \\]\n\n5. Divide the entire equation by 200 to simplify:\n   \\[\n   100A + 10M + C = 617\n   \\]\n\nNow, we need to find the values of \\( A \\), \\( M \\), and \\( C \\) such that the equation holds true and they are digits (0-9).\n\nLet's solve for \\( A \\), \\( M \\), and \\( C \\):\n\n- Since \\( 100A + 10M + C = 617 \\), \\( A \\) must be 6 because \\( 100A \\) is the largest term and 600 is the closest multiple of 100 to 617.\n- Substitute \\( A = 6 \\) into the equation:\n  \\[\n  100(6) + 10M + C = 617\n  \\]\n  \\[\n  600 + 10M + C = 617\n  \\]\n  \\[\n  10M + C = 17\n  \\]\n\n- Now, we need to find digits \\( M \\) and \\( C \\) such that \\( 10M + C = 17 \\). The only possible values are \\( M = 1 \\) and \\( C = 7 \\).\n\nThus, \\( A = 6 \\), \\( M = 1 \\), and \\( C = 7 \\).\n\nFinally, calculate \\( A + M + C \\):\n\\[\nA + M + C = 6 + 1 + 7 = 14\n\\]\n\nThe answer is \\( \\boxed{14} \\)."
"To solve this problem, we need to determine how many people are required to mow the lawn in 3 hours, given that 5 people can mow it in 12 hours. We will then find out how many additional people are needed.\n\nFirst, let's calculate the total amount of work required to mow the lawn. If 5 people can mow the lawn in 12 hours, the total work can be expressed as:\n\n\\[ \\text{Total work} = 5 \\text{ people} \\times 12 \\text{ hours} = 60 \\text{ person-hours} \\]\n\nThis means that mowing the lawn requires 60 person-hours of work.\n\nNow, we want to complete this work in 3 hours. Let \\( x \\) be the number of people needed to mow the lawn in 3 hours. The equation for the total work is:\n\n\\[ x \\text{ people} \\times 3 \\text{ hours} = 60 \\text{ person-hours} \\]\n\nSolving for \\( x \\):\n\n\\[ x \\times 3 = 60 \\]\n\n\\[ x = \\frac{60}{3} = 20 \\]\n\nSo, 20 people are needed to mow the lawn in 3 hours.\n\nSince we already have 5 people, the number of additional people needed is:\n\n\\[ 20 - 5 = 15 \\]\n\nTherefore, 15 additional people are needed to mow the lawn in 3 hours."
'To find \\(x^3-y^3\\), we can use the identity:\n\n\\[\nx^3-y^3 = (x-y)(x^2+xy+y^2)\n\\]\n\nWe are given:\n\n1. \\(x-y = 6\\)\n2. \\(x^2 + y^2 = 24\\)\n\nFirst, we need to find \\(xy\\). We can use the identity:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + y^2 = (x-y)^2 + 2xy\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the given values:\n\n\\[\n24 = 6^2 + 2xy\n\\]\n\n\\[\n24 = 36 + 2xy\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\(xy\\):\n\n\\[\n24 - 36 = 2xy\n\\]\n\n\\[\n-12 = 2xy\n\\]\n\n\\[\nxy = -6\n\\]\n\nNow, we have \\(x-y = 6\\), \\(x^2 + y^2 = 24\\), and \\(xy = -6\\).\n\nNext, we substitute these into the expression for \\(x^3-y^3\\):\n\n\\[\nx^3-y^3 = (x-y)(x^2+xy+y^2)\n\\]\n\nSubstitute the known values:\n\n\\[\nx^3-y^3 = 6 \\times (24 + (-6))\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx^3-y^3 = 6 \\times 18\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx^3-y^3 = 108\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(x^3-y^3\\) is \\(\\boxed{108}\\).'
'To evaluate the expression \\(\\sqrt[3]{12} \\times \\sqrt[3]{20} \\times \\sqrt[3]{15} \\times \\sqrt[3]{60}\\), we can use the property of cube roots that allows us to combine them into a single cube root:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt[3]{12} \\times \\sqrt[3]{20} \\times \\sqrt[3]{15} \\times \\sqrt[3]{60} = \\sqrt[3]{12 \\times 20 \\times 15 \\times 60}\n\\]\n\nNext, we calculate the product inside the cube root:\n\n1. **Prime Factorization**:\n   - \\(12 = 2^2 \\times 3\\)\n   - \\(20 = 2^2 \\times 5\\)\n   - \\(15 = 3 \\times 5\\)\n   - \\(60 = 2^2 \\times 3 \\times 5\\)\n\n2. **Combine Prime Factors**:\n   \\[\n   (2^2 \\times 3) \\times (2^2 \\times 5) \\times (3 \\times 5) \\times (2^2 \\times 3 \\times 5)\n   \\]\n\n3. **Simplify the Product**:\n   \\[\n   2^{2+2+2} \\times 3^{1+1+1} \\times 5^{1+1+1} = 2^6 \\times 3^3 \\times 5^3\n   \\]\n\nNow, we take the cube root of the simplified product:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt[3]{2^6 \\times 3^3 \\times 5^3} = 2^{6/3} \\times 3^{3/3} \\times 5^{3/3} = 2^2 \\times 3 \\times 5\n\\]\n\nFinally, we calculate the result:\n\n\\[\n2^2 \\times 3 \\times 5 = 4 \\times 3 \\times 5 = 12 \\times 5 = 60\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of the expression is \\(60\\).'
'To determine how many hours it would take Bob to travel \\( h \\) miles at his current rate, we start by understanding his rate of travel. Bob can travel \\( m \\) miles in \\( h \\) hours, which means his rate is:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Rate} = \\frac{m}{h} \\text{ miles per hour}\n\\]\n\nWe need to find the time it takes to travel \\( h \\) miles at this rate. The formula for time when distance and rate are known is:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Time} = \\frac{\\text{Distance}}{\\text{Rate}}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the given values into this formula, we have:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Time} = \\frac{h}{\\frac{m}{h}}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the expression:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Time} = \\frac{h \\cdot h}{m} = \\frac{h^2}{m}\n\\]\n\nTherefore, it would take Bob \\(\\frac{h^2}{m}\\) hours to travel \\( h \\) miles at his current rate. The answer is \\(\\frac{h^2}{m}\\).'
"To determine Cal O'Ree's weight at the end of ten weeks, we need to calculate his weight loss each week and apply it iteratively over the ten-week period. Cal starts with a weight of 244 pounds and loses 1% of his weight at the end of each week.\n\n1. **Initial Weight:** 244 pounds.\n\n2. **Weekly Weight Loss:** Each week, Cal loses 1% of his weight from the previous week. This means his weight at the end of each week is 99% of his weight at the end of the previous week.\n\n3. **Weight Calculation:**\n   - Week 1: \\( 244 \\times 0.99 = 241.56 \\) pounds\n   - Week 2: \\( 241.56 \\times 0.99 = 239.1444 \\) pounds\n   - Week 3: \\( 239.1444 \\times 0.99 = 236.753956 \\) pounds\n   - Week 4: \\( 236.753956 \\times 0.99 = 234.38641644 \\) pounds\n   - Week 5: \\( 234.38641644 \\times 0.99 = 232.0425522756 \\) pounds\n   - Week 6: \\( 232.0425522756 \\times 0.99 = 229.722126752844 \\) pounds\n   - Week 7: \\( 229.722126752844 \\times 0.99 = 227.42490548531556 \\) pounds\n   - Week 8: \\( 227.42490548531556 \\times 0.99 = 225.1506564304624 \\) pounds\n   - Week 9: \\( 225.1506564304624 \\times 0.99 = 222.89914986615777 \\) pounds\n   - Week 10: \\( 222.89914986615777 \\times 0.99 = 220.6701583674962 \\) pounds\n\n4. **Final Weight:** After ten weeks, Cal's weight is approximately 220.6701583674962 pounds.\n\n5. **Rounding:** Rounding 220.6701583674962 to the nearest whole number gives us 221 pounds.\n\nTherefore, Cal O'Ree expects to weigh approximately 221 pounds at the end of ten weeks. The answer is \\(\\boxed{221}\\)."
